Divine Attributes

The Impossibility of Seeing God's Essence
A logical argument using dichotomy to prove vision of God impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that God cannot be seen either entirely or partially because of His infinity and indivisibility.

Core Idea
God's infinite and indivisible nature makes vision of Him impossible.

The author presents a concise classification argument that has been central to Islamic theology. Before we can discuss whether vision of God is possible, we must establish the rational grounds. This passage lays out a simple dichotomy: if something is seen, it is either seen entirely or partially. Applying this to God leads to the conclusion that vision is impossible because neither option applies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: a dichotomy and a conclusion.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage states that a seen thing is either seen in its entirety or seen partially. Identify these two possibilities in the text.
3
Understand why each is impossible for God
The author explains that seeing God entirely is impossible because He is not finite (infinite), and seeing Him partially is impossible because He is not divisible or composed of parts.
These are the key attributes to grasp: infinity and indivisibility.
4
Grasp the logical conclusion
Since both possibilities are impossible, there is no third option. Therefore, vision of God is impossible. This is a complete logical deduction.
The conclusion is presented succinctly: 'when both possibilities are impossible, vision is impossible due to the absence of a third division.'
5
Reflect on the significance
Think about how this argument protects God's transcendence and why it is a foundational proof in Islamic theology against anthropomorphism.
This connects to the broader topic of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام من حيث ذات المرئي فنقول : المرئي إما أن يرى كله وإما أن يرى بعضه، ولا جائز أن يرى الله تعالى كله لأنه تعالى ليس بمتناه، ولا جائز أن يرى بعضه، لأنه تعالى ليس بمتبعض ولا متجزئ، وإذا امتنع الوجهان امتنعت الرؤية لانعدام القسم الثالث.
As for the discussion regarding the essence of the seen, we say: The seen is either seen in its entirety or seen partially. And it is not permissible that Allah the Exalted be seen entirely because He is not finite, and it is not permissible that He be seen partially because He is not divisible nor composed of parts. And when both possibilities are impossible, vision is impossible due to the absence of a third division.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage presents a classification argument. The author presents a dichotomy: if something is seen, it is either seen entirely or partially. Since God is infinite (not finite) and indivisible (not composed of parts), neither option applies. Therefore, vision of God is impossible because there is no third possibility.

Key Terms
ذات المرئي
متناه
متبعض
متجزئ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can be seen partially or in a limited way.
Correction: The author argues that seeing partially is impossible because God is indivisible and not composed of parts. Since there is no part to be seen, partial vision is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it impossible to see God?
A) Because He is too great
B) Because He cannot be seen entirely or partially due to His infinity and indivisibility
C) Because vision requires a body
D) Because He is hidden

Key Takeaway
God's infinity and indivisibility necessitate that He cannot be seen, as vision requires either seeing the whole or a part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have felt distant from God precisely because you cannot see Him, how does this logical argument challenge your expectation? Will you now embrace His invisibility as a sign of His majesty, and how will you actively seek closeness to an unseen God through His names and signs?
?
The proof shows that vision of God is impossible by its very nature — not because of any deficiency in you, but because of His infinite perfection. Does your heart truly rejoice in a God who is beyond physical perception, or does it secretly long for a tangible deity? What would it take for you to surrender that longing and worship Him as He truly is?
?
Imagine that tomorrow you encountered a being claiming to be God and visible. How would this argument prevent you from being deceived? How will you train your soul to trust in the unseen God described in revelation rather than fall for the temptation of visible gods?

The First Argument: Musa's Request Implies Visibility
First argument for the possibility of seeing Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Prophet Musa's request to see Allah implies that Allah is visible, and denying this would attribute ignorance to a prophet.

Core Idea
A prophet's request proves divine visibility; otherwise it would be ignorance.

The People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) begin their proof by examining the request of Prophet Musa to see Allah. This argument uses the principle that a prophet cannot be ignorant of his Creator, so Musa's request shows that seeing Allah is possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic and English of the first argument. Notice how the author states that Musa believed Allah is visible.
The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Understand the implication
If Allah were not visible, Musa's request would be based on ignorance, which is impossible for a prophet. Thus, visibility must be possible.
3
Reflect on the importance
This argument establishes a foundational point: the Quranic narrative itself supports the possibility of seeing Allah.
It is the first of five arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل أهل الحق على إثبات الرؤية: وأما أهل الحق فإنهم احتجوا بقول الله تعالى خبرًا عن موسى عليه السلام رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ الآية. والاستدلال بالآية من وجوه: أحدها: أن موسى عليه السلام اعتقد أن الله تعالى مرئي، ولو لم يكن مرئيا كان هذا منه جهلا بخالقه ونسبة الأنبياء إلى الجهل بالله كفر. الثاني: أنه تعالى قال: لَن تَرَينِي نَفَى رُؤْيَةَ مُوسَى إِيَّاهُ وَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ ذَاتَهُ لَيْسَ بِمَرْئِيٍّ فَإِنَّهُ مَا قَالَ لَسْتُ بِمَرْئِيٍّ بَلْ قَالَ لَن تَرَينِي وَلَوْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتُهُ مَرْئِيَّةً لَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَرْئِيٍّ إِذِ الْحَالَةُ كَانَتْ حَالَةَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ لأَنَّهُ عَلَى زَعْمِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْمُلْحِدِينَ جَهَلَ اللهَ تَعَالَى وَالْحِكْمَةُ تَقْتَضِي الْبَيَانَ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ. وَالثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: وَلَكِنِ انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي فَاللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَّقَ الرُّؤْيَةَ بِاسْتِقْرَارِ الْجَبَلِ وَاسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ مِنَ الْجَائِزَاتِ، وَالأَصْلُ أَنَّ تَعْلِيقَ الْفِعْلِ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى جَوَازِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُمْتَنِعُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى امْتِنَاعِهِ وَعَدَمِ تَكَوُّنِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُتَحَقِّقُ الْوُجُودِ تَحْقِيقٌ لَهُ، وَهَا هُنَا جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ وَهُوَ اسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ، وَدَلِيلُ جَوَازِ وُجُودِهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا أَخْبَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا لَا أَنَّهُ انْدَكَّ بِنَفْسِهِ، وَمَا أَوْجَدَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى كَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يُوجَدَ لَوْ لَمْ يُوجِدْهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى، إِذِ اللهُ تَعَالَى مُخْتَارٌ فِيمَا يَفْعَلُ، فَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْجَبَلَ دَكًّا بِاخْتِيَارِهِ، وَكَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يَفْعَلَ دَلَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ جَوَازُ وُجُودِهِ، فَكَانَ تَعْلِيقُ الرُّؤْيَةِ بِهِ دَلِيلَ كَوْنِهَا جَائِزَةً. الرَّابِعُ: أَنَّهُ لَمَّا سَأَلَ الرُّؤْيَةَ مَا أَيَّأَسَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا عَاتَبَهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ خَارِجًا عَنِ الْحِكْمَةِ لَعَاتَبَهُ كَمَا عَاتَبَ نُوحًا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِقَوْلِهِ: إِنِّي أَعِظُكَ أَن تَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَاهِلِينَ حَيْثُ سَأَلَ رَبَّهُ إِنْجَاءَ ابْنِهِ مِنَ الْغَرَقِ. وَكَمَا عَاتَبَ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى أَكْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: أَلَمْ أَنْهَكُمَا عَن تِلْكُمَا الشَّجَرَةِ بَلْ هَذَا أَوْلَى بِالْعِتَابِ، لِأَنَّ هَذَا لَوْ كَانَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِرَبِّهِ لَبَلَغَ رُتْبَةَ الْكُفْرِ وَذَلِكَ لَمْ يَبْلُغْ هَذِهِ الرُّتْبَةَ، وَحَيْثُ لَمْ يُعَاتِبْهُ وَلَمْ يُيَئِّسْهُ بَلْ أَطْمَعَهُ وَرَجَّاهُ حَيْثُ عَلَّقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ، دَلَّ أَنَّ الرُّؤْيَةَ جَائِزَةُ الْوُجُودِ. الْخَامِسُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ وَالتَّجَلِّي هُوَ الظُّهُورُ أَيْ فَلَمَّا ظَهَرَ رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ. كَذَا رَوَى الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ أَهْلِ التَّأْوِيلِ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: لَكِنْ لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِهِ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِ غَيْرِهِ. وَكَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ شَيْئًا مِنْ صِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ صِفَاتِ غَيْرِهِ، فَلَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ هَذَا أَنَّ كَانَ بَيْنَ اللهِ وَبَيْنَ الْجَبَلِ حِجَابٌ فَارْتَفَعَ الْحِجَابُ وَظَهَرَ لِلْجَبَلِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا مِمَّا لَا يَلِيقُ بِصِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى. مَعْنَى التَّجَلِّي فِي الْآيَةِ: يَقُولُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: فَإِنْ قِيلَ كَيْفَ يُرَى؟ قِيلَ بِلَا كَيْفٍ إِذِ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ تَكُونُ لِذِي صُورَةٍ بَلْ يُرَى بِلَا وَصْفِ قِيَامٍ وَقُعُودٍ وَاتِّكَاءٍ وَتَعَلُّقٍ وَاتِّصَالٍ وَانْفِصَالٍ وَمُقَابَلَةٍ وَمُدَابَرَةٍ وَقَصَرٍ وَطَوِيلٍ وَظُلْمَةٍ وَسَاكِنٍ وَمُتَحَرِّكٍ وَمُمَاسٍّ وَتَبَايُنٍ وَخَارِجٍ وَلَا مَعْنَى يَأْخُذُهُ الْوَهْمُ أَوْ يُقَدِّرُهُ الْعَقْلُ لِتَعَالِيهِ عَنْ ذَلِكَ.
The Proof of the People of Truth for Establishing the Vision: As for the People of Truth, they adduced the saying of Allah Almighty, reporting from Musa (peace be upon him): 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You' (7:143). The inference from the verse is in several aspects: First: that Musa (peace be upon him) believed that Allah Almighty is visible; if He were not visible, this would be ignorance of his Creator on his part, and attributing ignorance of Allah to prophets is disbelief. Second: that He Almighty said, 'You will not see Me' (7:143). He negated Musa's seeing Him, but He did not inform that His essence is not visible; for He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather said 'You will not see Me.' If His essence were not visible, He would have informed that it is not visible, for the situation was a situation of need for clarification, because according to the claim of these atheists, he (Musa) would be ignorant of Allah Almighty, and wisdom requires clarification when there is need for clarification. Third: that He Almighty said: 'But look at the mountain; if it should remain in its place, then you will see Me' (7:143). Allah Almighty conditioned vision upon the mountain's remaining, and the mountain's remaining is among contingent things. The principle is that conditioning an act upon what is possible in existence indicates its possibility; conditioning it upon what is impossible in existence indicates its impossibility and non-occurrence; and conditioning it upon what is actualized in existence confirms it. Here, it is possible in existence—that is, the mountain's remaining. The evidence for its possible existence is His saying: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level' (7:143). Allah Almighty informed that He made it level, not that it leveled itself. And what Allah Almighty brings into existence is possible not to exist if Allah Almighty did not bring it into existence, for Allah Almighty is choice in what He does. So when He made the mountain level by His choice, and it was possible for Him not to do so, that indicates its possibility of existence. Thus conditioning vision upon it is evidence that vision is possible. Fourth: that when he asked for vision, Allah Almighty did not make him despair of it nor rebuke him for it. If that had been ignorance of Allah Almighty on his part or outside wisdom, He would have rebuked him, just as He rebuked Noah (peace be upon him) with His saying: 'Indeed, I advise you lest you be among the ignorant' (11:46) when he asked his Lord to save his son from drowning. And just as He rebuked Adam (peace be upon him) for eating from the tree with His saying: 'Did I not forbid you both from that tree?' (7:22). Rather, this is more deserving of rebuke, because if this were ignorance of his Lord, it would reach the level of disbelief, whereas that did not reach this level. And since He did not rebuke him nor make him despair, but rather gave him hope and made him expect by conditioning it upon what is possible in existence, this indicates that vision is possible in existence. Fifth: that He Almighty said: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain' (7:143). Manifestation (tajalli) is appearance—that is, 'when his Lord appeared to the mountain.' Thus narrated Sheikh Abu Mansur from the people of interpretation. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: 'But one does not understand from His appearance what is understood from the appearance of others.' And we say likewise: that nothing of the attributes of Allah Almighty is understood from it what is understood from the attributes of others. So it is not understood from this that there was a veil between Allah and the mountain and the veil was lifted and He appeared to the mountain, for this is not befitting the attributes of Allah Almighty. The meaning of tajalli in the verse: Abu Mansur says: 'If it is said: How is He seen? It is said: Without modality (bila kayf), for modality pertains to that which has form. Rather, He is seen without the description of standing, sitting, leaning, attachment, connection, separation, facing, backing, shortness, length, darkness, stillness, motion, contact, separation, being outside, nor any meaning that imagination takes or the intellect conceives, for He is exalted above that.'
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the Sunni theologians for the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the Quranic story of Prophet Musa (peace be upon him). The author enumerates five distinct arguments from the verse (7:143). The first argument is that Prophet Musa asked to see Allah, and his request presupposes that Allah is visible; if not, Musa would have been ignorant of his Creator, which is impossible for a prophet. The second argument focuses on Allah's response 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me); He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather negated Musa's seeing at that moment, implying that vision is possible in itself. The third argument is based on the conditional phrase 'if the mountain remains in its place, then you will see Me.' Since the mountain's remaining is a contingent possibility, conditioning vision upon a possible act indicates that vision itself is possible. The author explains that Allah made the mountain level (dakkan) by His own act, showing that the mountain's remaining was possible but Allah chose to destroy it. The fourth argument notes that Allah did not rebuke Musa for asking, unlike His rebuke to Noah and Adam for lesser matters; this leniency indicates that the request was not improper and vision is possible. The fifth argument examines the term 'tajalla' (manifested) to the mountain, explaining that it signifies appearance but without anthropomorphic interpretation; rather, it is an appearance befitting Allah's majesty, without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a quotation from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi emphasizing that divine attributes are not understood by analogy with created beings.

Key Terms
رؤية
مرئي
جهل
نسبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence if Allah were not visible according to the first argument?
A) Musa would have been mistaken but not sinful.
B) Musa would have been ignorant of his Creator, which is disbelief.
C) The request would still be valid as a test.
D) The Quran would not have recorded the story.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Musa's request to see Allah proves that seeing Allah is possible, because a prophet cannot be ignorant of his Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that prophets are free from ignorance about Allah, how would that change the way you receive their words and actions, especially regarding matters of the unseen?
?
When you make a request of Allah, do you do so with the same certainty that it is possible and good? What would it take for you to reach that level of conviction?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
The Second Argument: 'Lan Tarani' Negates Sight, Not Visibility
Second argument based on the wording of Allah's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's statement 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me) negates actual vision at a specific time, not the possibility of seeing Him in essence.

Core Idea
Allah said 'you will not see Me,' not 'I am not visible.'

The second argument focuses on the precise wording of Allah's response to Musa. The author argues that the phrase 'lan tarani' does not declare that Allah's essence is invisible; it only says that Musa will not see Him at that moment. This careful distinction supports the possibility of vision.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text
Notice the exact phrasing: لَن تَرَينِي (you will not see Me) versus لَسْتُ بِمَرْئِيٍّ (I am not visible).
The difference is subtle but crucial.
2
Understand the implication of the wording
If Allah had said 'I am not visible,' that would negate possibility. But He only negated Musa's seeing at that time. This implies visibility is possible.
3
Consider the context of need for clarification
The author argues that if vision were impossible, Allah would have made that clear, especially when there was a need to correct a potential misunderstanding.
This refutes the atheists' claim that Musa was ignorant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل أهل الحق على إثبات الرؤية: وأما أهل الحق فإنهم احتجوا بقول الله تعالى خبرًا عن موسى عليه السلام رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ الآية. والاستدلال بالآية من وجوه: أحدها: أن موسى عليه السلام اعتقد أن الله تعالى مرئي، ولو لم يكن مرئيا كان هذا منه جهلا بخالقه ونسبة الأنبياء إلى الجهل بالله كفر. الثاني: أنه تعالى قال: لَن تَرَينِي نَفَى رُؤْيَةَ مُوسَى إِيَّاهُ وَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ ذَاتَهُ لَيْسَ بِمَرْئِيٍّ فَإِنَّهُ مَا قَالَ لَسْتُ بِمَرْئِيٍّ بَلْ قَالَ لَن تَرَينِي وَلَوْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتُهُ مَرْئِيَّةً لَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَرْئِيٍّ إِذِ الْحَالَةُ كَانَتْ حَالَةَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ لأَنَّهُ عَلَى زَعْمِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْمُلْحِدِينَ جَهَلَ اللهَ تَعَالَى وَالْحِكْمَةُ تَقْتَضِي الْبَيَانَ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ. وَالثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: وَلَكِنِ انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي فَاللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَّقَ الرُّؤْيَةَ بِاسْتِقْرَارِ الْجَبَلِ وَاسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ مِنَ الْجَائِزَاتِ، وَالأَصْلُ أَنَّ تَعْلِيقَ الْفِعْلِ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى جَوَازِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُمْتَنِعُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى امْتِنَاعِهِ وَعَدَمِ تَكَوُّنِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُتَحَقِّقُ الْوُجُودِ تَحْقِيقٌ لَهُ، وَهَا هُنَا جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ وَهُوَ اسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ، وَدَلِيلُ جَوَازِ وُجُودِهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا أَخْبَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا لَا أَنَّهُ انْدَكَّ بِنَفْسِهِ، وَمَا أَوْجَدَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى كَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يُوجَدَ لَوْ لَمْ يُوجِدْهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى، إِذِ اللهُ تَعَالَى مُخْتَارٌ فِيمَا يَفْعَلُ، فَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْجَبَلَ دَكًّا بِاخْتِيَارِهِ، وَكَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يَفْعَلَ دَلَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ جَوَازُ وُجُودِهِ، فَكَانَ تَعْلِيقُ الرُّؤْيَةِ بِهِ دَلِيلَ كَوْنِهَا جَائِزَةً. الرَّابِعُ: أَنَّهُ لَمَّا سَأَلَ الرُّؤْيَةَ مَا أَيَّأَسَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا عَاتَبَهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ خَارِجًا عَنِ الْحِكْمَةِ لَعَاتَبَهُ كَمَا عَاتَبَ نُوحًا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِقَوْلِهِ: إِنِّي أَعِظُكَ أَن تَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَاهِلِينَ حَيْثُ سَأَلَ رَبَّهُ إِنْجَاءَ ابْنِهِ مِنَ الْغَرَقِ. وَكَمَا عَاتَبَ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى أَكْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: أَلَمْ أَنْهَكُمَا عَن تِلْكُمَا الشَّجَرَةِ بَلْ هَذَا أَوْلَى بِالْعِتَابِ، لِأَنَّ هَذَا لَوْ كَانَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِرَبِّهِ لَبَلَغَ رُتْبَةَ الْكُفْرِ وَذَلِكَ لَمْ يَبْلُغْ هَذِهِ الرُّتْبَةَ، وَحَيْثُ لَمْ يُعَاتِبْهُ وَلَمْ يُيَئِّسْهُ بَلْ أَطْمَعَهُ وَرَجَّاهُ حَيْثُ عَلَّقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ، دَلَّ أَنَّ الرُّؤْيَةَ جَائِزَةُ الْوُجُودِ. الْخَامِسُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ وَالتَّجَلِّي هُوَ الظُّهُورُ أَيْ فَلَمَّا ظَهَرَ رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ. كَذَا رَوَى الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ أَهْلِ التَّأْوِيلِ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: لَكِنْ لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِهِ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِ غَيْرِهِ. وَكَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ شَيْئًا مِنْ صِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ صِفَاتِ غَيْرِهِ، فَلَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ هَذَا أَنَّ كَانَ بَيْنَ اللهِ وَبَيْنَ الْجَبَلِ حِجَابٌ فَارْتَفَعَ الْحِجَابُ وَظَهَرَ لِلْجَبَلِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا مِمَّا لَا يَلِيقُ بِصِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى. مَعْنَى التَّجَلِّي فِي الْآيَةِ: يَقُولُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: فَإِنْ قِيلَ كَيْفَ يُرَى؟ قِيلَ بِلَا كَيْفٍ إِذِ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ تَكُونُ لِذِي صُورَةٍ بَلْ يُرَى بِلَا وَصْفِ قِيَامٍ وَقُعُودٍ وَاتِّكَاءٍ وَتَعَلُّقٍ وَاتِّصَالٍ وَانْفِصَالٍ وَمُقَابَلَةٍ وَمُدَابَرَةٍ وَقَصَرٍ وَطَوِيلٍ وَظُلْمَةٍ وَسَاكِنٍ وَمُتَحَرِّكٍ وَمُمَاسٍّ وَتَبَايُنٍ وَخَارِجٍ وَلَا مَعْنَى يَأْخُذُهُ الْوَهْمُ أَوْ يُقَدِّرُهُ الْعَقْلُ لِتَعَالِيهِ عَنْ ذَلِكَ.
The Proof of the People of Truth for Establishing the Vision: As for the People of Truth, they adduced the saying of Allah Almighty, reporting from Musa (peace be upon him): 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You' (7:143). The inference from the verse is in several aspects: First: that Musa (peace be upon him) believed that Allah Almighty is visible; if He were not visible, this would be ignorance of his Creator on his part, and attributing ignorance of Allah to prophets is disbelief. Second: that He Almighty said, 'You will not see Me' (7:143). He negated Musa's seeing Him, but He did not inform that His essence is not visible; for He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather said 'You will not see Me.' If His essence were not visible, He would have informed that it is not visible, for the situation was a situation of need for clarification, because according to the claim of these atheists, he (Musa) would be ignorant of Allah Almighty, and wisdom requires clarification when there is need for clarification. Third: that He Almighty said: 'But look at the mountain; if it should remain in its place, then you will see Me' (7:143). Allah Almighty conditioned vision upon the mountain's remaining, and the mountain's remaining is among contingent things. The principle is that conditioning an act upon what is possible in existence indicates its possibility; conditioning it upon what is impossible in existence indicates its impossibility and non-occurrence; and conditioning it upon what is actualized in existence confirms it. Here, it is possible in existence—that is, the mountain's remaining. The evidence for its possible existence is His saying: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level' (7:143). Allah Almighty informed that He made it level, not that it leveled itself. And what Allah Almighty brings into existence is possible not to exist if Allah Almighty did not bring it into existence, for Allah Almighty is choice in what He does. So when He made the mountain level by His choice, and it was possible for Him not to do so, that indicates its possibility of existence. Thus conditioning vision upon it is evidence that vision is possible. Fourth: that when he asked for vision, Allah Almighty did not make him despair of it nor rebuke him for it. If that had been ignorance of Allah Almighty on his part or outside wisdom, He would have rebuked him, just as He rebuked Noah (peace be upon him) with His saying: 'Indeed, I advise you lest you be among the ignorant' (11:46) when he asked his Lord to save his son from drowning. And just as He rebuked Adam (peace be upon him) for eating from the tree with His saying: 'Did I not forbid you both from that tree?' (7:22). Rather, this is more deserving of rebuke, because if this were ignorance of his Lord, it would reach the level of disbelief, whereas that did not reach this level. And since He did not rebuke him nor make him despair, but rather gave him hope and made him expect by conditioning it upon what is possible in existence, this indicates that vision is possible in existence. Fifth: that He Almighty said: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain' (7:143). Manifestation (tajalli) is appearance—that is, 'when his Lord appeared to the mountain.' Thus narrated Sheikh Abu Mansur from the people of interpretation. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: 'But one does not understand from His appearance what is understood from the appearance of others.' And we say likewise: that nothing of the attributes of Allah Almighty is understood from it what is understood from the attributes of others. So it is not understood from this that there was a veil between Allah and the mountain and the veil was lifted and He appeared to the mountain, for this is not befitting the attributes of Allah Almighty. The meaning of tajalli in the verse: Abu Mansur says: 'If it is said: How is He seen? It is said: Without modality (bila kayf), for modality pertains to that which has form. Rather, He is seen without the description of standing, sitting, leaning, attachment, connection, separation, facing, backing, shortness, length, darkness, stillness, motion, contact, separation, being outside, nor any meaning that imagination takes or the intellect conceives, for He is exalted above that.'
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the Sunni theologians for the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the Quranic story of Prophet Musa (peace be upon him). The author enumerates five distinct arguments from the verse (7:143). The first argument is that Prophet Musa asked to see Allah, and his request presupposes that Allah is visible; if not, Musa would have been ignorant of his Creator, which is impossible for a prophet. The second argument focuses on Allah's response 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me); He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather negated Musa's seeing at that moment, implying that vision is possible in itself. The third argument is based on the conditional phrase 'if the mountain remains in its place, then you will see Me.' Since the mountain's remaining is a contingent possibility, conditioning vision upon a possible act indicates that vision itself is possible. The author explains that Allah made the mountain level (dakkan) by His own act, showing that the mountain's remaining was possible but Allah chose to destroy it. The fourth argument notes that Allah did not rebuke Musa for asking, unlike His rebuke to Noah and Adam for lesser matters; this leniency indicates that the request was not improper and vision is possible. The fifth argument examines the term 'tajalla' (manifested) to the mountain, explaining that it signifies appearance but without anthropomorphic interpretation; rather, it is an appearance befitting Allah's majesty, without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a quotation from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi emphasizing that divine attributes are not understood by analogy with created beings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'lan tarani' proves vision is absolutely impossible.
Correction: The phrase only negates vision at that specific moment, not the possibility in essence. Allah did not say 'I am not visible.'

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, why did Allah not say 'I am not visible'?
A) Because it would be incorrect grammar.
B) Because He wanted to indicate that vision is possible.
C) Because Musa did not deserve a direct answer.
D) Because the context did not require clarification.

Key Takeaway
Allah's response 'lan tarani' negates a specific instance of seeing, not the possibility of seeing Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you focus on the exact words Allah chose, or do you sometimes assume meanings that are not there? How can you train yourself to be more precise with Allah's speech, especially when it comes to matters of faith?
?
Allah said 'you will not see Me' but not 'I am not visible.' Are there areas in your life where you have added restrictions or impossibilities that Allah did not place? For example, in your relationship with Him or your expectations of His mercy? What would it take to align your assumptions with what He actually said?
?
Musa (AS) longed to see Allah in this world, and Allah postponed that vision. Do you have a deep desire to see Allah in the Hereafter? How does knowing that He is visible in principle strengthen your hope and motivate your worship today?

The Third Argument: The Conditional Clause Indicates Possibility
Third argument based on conditional logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's conditional statement 'if the mountain remains, you will see Me' indicates that vision is possible because the condition is a contingent event.

Core Idea
Conditioning vision on a possible act proves its possibility.

The third argument uses logical reasoning based on the conditional phrase in the verse. The principle is that when an action is conditioned upon something that is possible, the action itself is possible. Since the mountain's remaining is possible, vision is possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Notice the conditional: 'If the mountain remains, then you will see Me.' Also note the general principle introduced.
The author distinguishes three types of conditions: possible, impossible, and actual.
2
Understand the principle
If an action depends on a possible event, the action is possible. If on an impossible event, the action is impossible. If on an actual event, the action is confirmed.
This is a standard kalam logical principle.
3
Apply the principle to the verse
The mountain's remaining is possible (as shown by the fact that Allah made it level, so it could have remained had Allah not acted). Therefore, vision is possible.
Allah's action of making the mountain level shows the mountain's remaining was within possibility.

دليل أهل الحق على إثبات الرؤية: وأما أهل الحق فإنهم احتجوا بقول الله تعالى خبرًا عن موسى عليه السلام رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ الآية. والاستدلال بالآية من وجوه: أحدها: أن موسى عليه السلام اعتقد أن الله تعالى مرئي، ولو لم يكن مرئيا كان هذا منه جهلا بخالقه ونسبة الأنبياء إلى الجهل بالله كفر. الثاني: أنه تعالى قال: لَن تَرَينِي نَفَى رُؤْيَةَ مُوسَى إِيَّاهُ وَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ ذَاتَهُ لَيْسَ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ لأَنَّهُ عَلَى زَعْمِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْمُلْحِدِينَ جَهَلَ اللهَ تَعَالَى وَالْحِكْمَةُ تَقْتَضِي الْبَيَانَ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ. وَالثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: وَلَكِنِ انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي فَاللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَّقَ الرُّؤْيَةَ بِاسْتِقْرَارِ الْجَبَلِ وَاسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ مِنَ الْجَائِزَاتِ، وَالأَصْلُ أَنَّ تَعْلِيقَ الْفِعْلِ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى جَوَازِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُمْتَنِعُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى امْتِنَاعِهِ وَعَدَمِ تَكَوُّنِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُتَحَقِّقُ الْوُجُودِ تَحْقِيقٌ لَهُ، وَهَا هُنَا جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ وَهُوَ اسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ، وَدَلِيلُ جَوَازِ وُجُودِهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا أَخْبَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا لَا أَنَّهُ انْدَكَّ بِنَفْسِهِ، وَمَا أَوْجَدَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى كَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يُوجَدَ لَوْ لَمْ يُوجِدْهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى، إِذِ اللهُ تَعَالَى مُخْتَارٌ فِيمَا يَفْعَلُ، فَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْجَبَلَ دَكًّا بِاخْتِيَارِهِ، وَكَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يَفْعَلَ دَلَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ جَوَازُ وُجُودِهِ، فَكَانَ تَعْلِيقُ الرُّؤْيَةِ بِهِ دَلِيلَ كَوْنِهَا جَائِزَةً. الرَّابِعُ: أَنَّهُ لَمَّا سَأَلَ الرُّؤْيَةَ مَا أَيَّأَسَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا عَاتَبَهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ خَارِجًا عَنِ الْحِكْمَةِ لَعَاتَبَهُ كَمَا عَاتَبَ نُوحًا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِقَوْلِهِ: إِنِّي أَعِظُكَ أَن تَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَاهِلِينَ حَيْثُ سَأَلَ رَبَّهُ إِنْجَاءَ ابْنِهِ مِنَ الْغَرَقِ. وَكَمَا عَاتَبَ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى أَكْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: أَلَمْ أَنْهَكُمَا عَن تِلْكُمَا الشَّجَرَةِ بَلْ هَذَا أَوْلَى بِالْعِتَابِ، لِأَنَّ هَذَا لَوْ كَانَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِرَبِّهِ لَبَلَغَ رُتْبَةَ الْكُفْرِ وَذَلِكَ لَمْ يَبْلُغْ هَذِهِ الرُّتْبَةَ، وَحَيْثُ لَمْ يُعَاتِبْهُ وَلَمْ يُيَئِّسْهُ بَلْ أَطْمَعَهُ وَرَجَّاهُ حَيْثُ عَلَّقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ، دَلَّ أَنَّ الرُّؤْيَةَ جَائِزَةُ الْوُجُودِ. الْخَامِسُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ وَالتَّجَلِّي هُوَ الظُّهُورُ أَيْ فَلَمَّا ظَهَرَ رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ. كَذَا رَوَى الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ أَهْلِ التَّأْوِيلِ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: لَكِنْ لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِهِ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِ غَيْرِهِ. وَكَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ شَيْئًا مِنْ صِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ صِفَاتِ غَيْرِهِ، فَلَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ هَذَا أَنَّ كَانَ بَيْنَ اللهِ وَبَيْنَ الْجَبَلِ حِجَابٌ فَارْتَفَعَ الْحِجَابُ وَظَهَرَ لِلْجَبَلِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا مِمَّا لَا يَلِيقُ بِصِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى. مَعْنَى التَّجَلِّي فِي الْآيَةِ: يَقُولُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: فَإِنْ قِيلَ كَيْفَ يُرَى؟ قِيلَ بِلَا كَيْفٍ إِذِ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ تَكُونُ لِذِي صُورَةٍ بَلْ يُرَى بِلَا وَصْفِ قِيَامٍ وَقُعُودٍ وَاتِّكَاءٍ وَتَعَلُّقٍ وَاتِّصَالٍ وَانْفِصَالٍ وَمُقَابَلَةٍ وَمُدَابَرَةٍ وَقَصَرٍ وَطَوِيلٍ وَظُلْمَةٍ وَسَاكِنٍ وَمُتَحَرِّكٍ وَمُمَاسٍّ وَتَبَايُنٍ وَخَارِجٍ وَلَا مَعْنَى يَأْخُذُهُ الْوَهْمُ أَوْ يُقَدِّرُهُ الْعَقْلُ لِتَعَالِيهِ عَنْ ذَلِكَ.
The Proof of the People of Truth for Establishing the Vision: As for the People of Truth, they adduced the saying of Allah Almighty, reporting from Musa (peace be upon him): 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You' (7:143). The inference from the verse is in several aspects: First: that Musa (peace be upon him) believed that Allah Almighty is visible; if He were not visible, this would be ignorance of his Creator on his part, and attributing ignorance of Allah to prophets is disbelief. Second: that He Almighty said, 'You will not see Me' (7:143). He negated Musa's seeing Him, but He did not inform that His essence is not visible; for He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather said 'You will not see Me.' If His essence were not visible, He would have informed that it is not visible, for the situation was a situation of need for clarification, because according to the claim of these atheists, he (Musa) would be ignorant of Allah Almighty, and wisdom requires clarification when there is need for clarification. Third: that He Almighty said: 'But look at the mountain; if it should remain in its place, then you will see Me' (7:143). Allah Almighty conditioned vision upon the mountain's remaining, and the mountain's remaining is among contingent things. The principle is that conditioning an act upon what is possible in existence indicates its possibility; conditioning it upon what is impossible in existence indicates its impossibility and non-occurrence; and conditioning it upon what is actualized in existence confirms it. Here, it is possible in existence—that is, the mountain's remaining. The evidence for its possible existence is His saying: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level' (7:143). Allah Almighty informed that He made it level, not that it leveled itself. And what Allah Almighty brings into existence is possible not to exist if Allah Almighty did not bring it into existence, for Allah Almighty is choice in what He does. So when He made the mountain level by His choice, and it was possible for Him not to do so, that indicates its possibility of existence. Thus conditioning vision upon it is evidence that vision is possible. Fourth: that when he asked for vision, Allah Almighty did not make him despair of it nor rebuke him for it. If that had been ignorance of Allah Almighty on his part or outside wisdom, He would have rebuked him, just as He rebuked Noah (peace be upon him) with His saying: 'Indeed, I advise you lest you be among the ignorant' (11:46) when he asked his Lord to save his son from drowning. And just as He rebuked Adam (peace be upon him) for eating from the tree with His saying: 'Did I not forbid you both from that tree?' (7:22). Rather, this is more deserving of rebuke, because if this were ignorance of his Lord, it would reach the level of disbelief, whereas that did not reach this level. And since He did not rebuke him nor make him despair, but rather gave him hope and made him expect by conditioning it upon what is possible in existence, this indicates that vision is possible in existence. Fifth: that He Almighty said: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain' (7:143). Manifestation (tajalli) is appearance—that is, 'when his Lord appeared to the mountain.' Thus narrated Sheikh Abu Mansur from the people of interpretation. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: 'But one does not understand from His appearance what is understood from the appearance of others.' And we say likewise: that nothing of the attributes of Allah Almighty is understood from it what is understood from the attributes of others. So it is not understood from this that there was a veil between Allah and the mountain and the veil was lifted and He appeared to the mountain, for this is not befitting the attributes of Allah Almighty. The meaning of tajalli in the verse: Abu Mansur says: 'If it is said: How is He seen? It is said: Without modality (bila kayf), for modality pertains to that which has form. Rather, He is seen without the description of standing, sitting, leaning, attachment, connection, separation, facing, backing, shortness, length, darkness, stillness, motion, contact, separation, being outside, nor any meaning that imagination takes or the intellect conceives, for He is exalted above that.'
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the Sunni theologians for the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the Quranic story of Prophet Musa (peace be upon him). The author enumerates five distinct arguments from the verse (7:143). The first argument is that Prophet Musa asked to see Allah, and his request presupposes that Allah is visible; if not, Musa would have been ignorant of his Creator, which is impossible for a prophet. The second argument focuses on Allah's response 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me); He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather negated Musa's seeing at that moment, implying that vision is possible in itself. The third argument is based on the conditional phrase 'if the mountain remains in its place, then you will see Me.' Since the mountain's remaining is a contingent possibility, conditioning vision upon a possible act indicates that vision itself is possible. The author explains that Allah made the mountain level (dakkan) by His own act, showing that the mountain's remaining was possible but Allah chose to destroy it. The fourth argument notes that Allah did not rebuke Musa for asking, unlike His rebuke to Noah and Adam for lesser matters; this leniency indicates that the request was not improper and vision is possible. The fifth argument examines the term 'tajalla' (manifested) to the mountain, explaining that it signifies appearance but without anthropomorphic interpretation; rather, it is an appearance befitting Allah's majesty, without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a quotation from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi emphasizing that divine attributes are not understood by analogy with created beings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the principle of conditioning assert about an act conditioned on a possible event?
A) The act is impossible.
B) The act is possible.
C) The act is actual.
D) The act is necessary.

Key Takeaway
The conditional structure in the verse proves vision is possible because the condition is a contingent event.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The principle says that conditioning an act upon an impossible event makes the act impossible. Where in your life have you conditioned your faith or obedience on something you thought was impossible, only to realize that Allah's power makes all things possible? What specific step will you take this week to trust in His ability over your perceived impossibilities?
?
Allah's choice to destroy the mountain shows His absolute freedom. Are there areas in your life where you try to limit Allah's freedom by assuming He must act a certain way? Write down one assumption you hold about Allah that this lesson challenges, and commit to surrendering it.
?
The mountain's remaining was possible because Allah could have left it. How does this truth affect your understanding of divine mercy and justice? What one change in your daily worship will reflect your belief that nothing is impossible for Allah?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
The Fourth Argument: Absence of Rebuke Indicates Permissibility
Fourth argument based on divine silence on rebuke.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's lack of rebuke for Musa's request demonstrates that seeking vision is not improper and therefore vision is possible.

Core Idea
Allah did not rebuke Musa, unlike other prophets for lesser requests.

The fourth argument compares Musa's request with those of other prophets. Allah rebuked Noah and Adam for their requests, but He did not rebuke Musa. This indicates that Musa's request was valid and that vision is something permissible to seek.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the comparisons
The author mentions the rebukes of Noah and Adam. Compare their situations with Musa's.
Noah's request was to save his son, Adam's was eating from the tree.
2
Understand why rebuke would be expected
If Musa's request were improper (ignorance), Allah would have rebuked him as He did with others for lesser faults.
The author argues that this request would be even worse than the others if it were ignorance.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since there was no rebuke and even encouragement (hope), the request must be acceptable and vision possible.

دليل أهل الحق على إثبات الرؤية: وأما أهل الحق فإنهم احتجوا بقول الله تعالى خبرًا عن موسى عليه السلام رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ الآية. والاستدلال بالآية من وجوه: أحدها: أن موسى عليه السلام اعتقد أن الله تعالى مرئي، ولو لم يكن مرئيا كان هذا منه جهلا بخالقه ونسبة الأنبياء إلى الجهل بالله كفر. الثاني: أنه تعالى قال: لَن تَرَينِي نَفَى رُؤْيَةَ مُوسَى إِيَّاهُ وَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ ذَاتَهُ لَيْسَ بِمَرْئِيٍّ فَإِنَّهُ مَا قَالَ لَسْتُ بِمَرْئِيٍّ بَلْ قَالَ لَن تَرَينِي وَلَوْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتُهُ مَرْئِيَّةً لَمَا أَخْبَرَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَرْئِيٍّ إِذِ الْحَالَةُ كَانَتْ حَالَةَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ لأَنَّهُ عَلَى زَعْمِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْمُلْحِدِينَ جَهَلَ اللهَ تَعَالَى وَالْحِكْمَةُ تَقْتَضِي الْبَيَانَ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ. وَالثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: وَلَكِنِ انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي فَاللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَّقَ الرُّؤْيَةَ بِاسْتِقْرَارِ الْجَبَلِ وَاسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ مِنَ الْجَائِزَاتِ، وَالأَصْلُ أَنَّ تَعْلِيقَ الْفِعْلِ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى جَوَازِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُمْتَنِعُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى امْتِنَاعِهِ وَعَدَمِ تَكَوُّنِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُتَحَقِّقُ الْوُجُودِ تَحْقِيقٌ لَهُ، وَهَا هُنَا جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ وَهُوَ اسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ، وَدَلِيلُ جَوَازِ وُجُودِهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا أَخْبَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا لَا أَنَّهُ انْدَكَّ بِنَفْسِهِ، وَمَا أَوْجَدَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى كَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يُوجَدَ لَوْ لَمْ يُوجِدْهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى، إِذِ اللهُ تَعَالَى مُخْتَارٌ فِيمَا يَفْعَلُ، فَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْجَبَلَ دَكًّا بِاخْتِيَارِهِ، وَكَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يَفْعَلَ دَلَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ جَوَازُ وُجُودِهِ، فَكَانَ تَعْلِيقُ الرُّؤْيَةِ بِهِ دَلِيلَ كَوْنِهَا جَائِزَةً. الرَّابِعُ: أَنَّهُ لَمَّا سَأَلَ الرُّؤْيَةَ مَا أَيَّأَسَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا عَاتَبَهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ خَارِجًا عَنِ الْحِكْمَةِ لَعَاتَبَهُ كَمَا عَاتَبَ نُوحًا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِقَوْلِهِ: إِنِّي أَعِظُكَ أَن تَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَاهِلِينَ حَيْثُ سَأَلَ رَبَّهُ إِنْجَاءَ ابْنِهِ مِنَ الْغَرَقِ. وَكَمَا عَاتَبَ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى أَكْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: أَلَمْ أَنْهَكُمَا عَن تِلْكُمَا الشَّجَرَةِ بَلْ هَذَا أَوْلَى بِالْعِتَابِ، لِأَنَّ هَذَا لَوْ كَانَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِرَبِّهِ لَبَلَغَ رُتْبَةَ الْكُفْرِ وَذَلِكَ لَمْ يَبْلُغْ هَذِهِ الرُّتْبَةَ، وَحَيْثُ لَمْ يُعَاتِبْهُ وَلَمْ يُيَئِّسْهُ بَلْ أَطْمَعَهُ وَرَجَّاهُ حَيْثُ عَلَّقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ، دَلَّ أَنَّ الرُّؤْيَةَ جَائِزَةُ الْوُجُودِ. الْخَامِسُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ وَالتَّجَلِّي هُوَ الظُّهُورُ أَيْ فَلَمَّا ظَهَرَ رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ. كَذَا رَوَى الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ أَهْلِ التَّأْوِيلِ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: لَكِنْ لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِهِ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِ غَيْرِهِ. وَكَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ شَيْئًا مِنْ صِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ صِفَاتِ غَيْرِهِ، فَلَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ هَذَا أَنَّ كَانَ بَيْنَ اللهِ وَبَيْنَ الْجَبَلِ حِجَابٌ فَارْتَفَعَ الْحِجَابُ وَظَهَرَ لِلْجَبَلِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا مِمَّا لَا يَلِيقُ بِصِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى. مَعْنَى التَّجَلِّي فِي الْآيَةِ: يَقُولُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: فَإِنْ قِيلَ كَيْفَ يُرَى؟ قِيلَ بِلَا كَيْفٍ إِذِ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ تَكُونُ لِذِي صُورَةٍ بَلْ يُرَى بِلَا وَصْفِ قِيَامٍ وَقُعُودٍ وَاتِّكَاءٍ وَتَعَلُّقٍ وَاتِّصَالٍ وَانْفِصَالٍ وَمُقَابَلَةٍ وَمُدَابَرَةٍ وَقَصَرٍ وَطَوِيلٍ وَظُلْمَةٍ وَسَاكِنٍ وَمُتَحَرِّكٍ وَمُمَاسٍّ وَتَبَايُنٍ وَخَارِجٍ وَلَا مَعْنَى يَأْخُذُهُ الْوَهْمُ أَوْ يُقَدِّرُهُ الْعَقْلُ لِتَعَالِيهِ عَنْ ذَلِكَ.
The Proof of the People of Truth for Establishing the Vision: As for the People of Truth, they adduced the saying of Allah Almighty, reporting from Musa (peace be upon him): 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You' (7:143). The inference from the verse is in several aspects: First: that Musa (peace be upon him) believed that Allah Almighty is visible; if He were not visible, this would be ignorance of his Creator on his part, and attributing ignorance of Allah to prophets is disbelief. Second: that He Almighty said, 'You will not see Me' (7:143). He negated Musa's seeing Him, but He did not inform that His essence is not visible; for He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather said 'You will not see Me.' If His essence were not visible, He would have informed that it is not visible, for the situation was a situation of need for clarification, because according to the claim of these atheists, he (Musa) would be ignorant of Allah Almighty, and wisdom requires clarification when there is need for clarification. Third: that He Almighty said: 'But look at the mountain; if it should remain in its place, then you will see Me' (7:143). Allah Almighty conditioned vision upon the mountain's remaining, and the mountain's remaining is among contingent things. The principle is that conditioning an act upon what is possible in existence indicates its possibility; conditioning it upon what is impossible in existence indicates its impossibility and non-occurrence; and conditioning it upon what is actualized in existence confirms it. Here, it is possible in existence—that is, the mountain's remaining. The evidence for its possible existence is His saying: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level' (7:143). Allah Almighty informed that He made it level, not that it leveled itself. And what Allah Almighty brings into existence is possible not to exist if Allah Almighty did not bring it into existence, for Allah Almighty is choice in what He does. So when He made the mountain level by His choice, and it was possible for Him not to do so, that indicates its possibility of existence. Thus conditioning vision upon it is evidence that vision is possible. Fourth: that when he asked for vision, Allah Almighty did not make him despair of it nor rebuke him for it. If that had been ignorance of Allah Almighty on his part or outside wisdom, He would have rebuked him, just as He rebuked Noah (peace be upon him) with His saying: 'Indeed, I advise you lest you be among the ignorant' (11:46) when he asked his Lord to save his son from drowning. And just as He rebuked Adam (peace be upon him) for eating from the tree with His saying: 'Did I not forbid you both from that tree?' (7:22). Rather, this is more deserving of rebuke, because if this were ignorance of his Lord, it would reach the level of disbelief, whereas that did not reach this level. And since He did not rebuke him nor make him despair, but rather gave him hope and made him expect by conditioning it upon what is possible in existence, this indicates that vision is possible in existence. Fifth: that He Almighty said: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain' (7:143). Manifestation (tajalli) is appearance—that is, 'when his Lord appeared to the mountain.' Thus narrated Sheikh Abu Mansur from the people of interpretation. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: 'But one does not understand from His appearance what is understood from the appearance of others.' And we say likewise: that nothing of the attributes of Allah Almighty is understood from it what is understood from the attributes of others. So it is not understood from this that there was a veil between Allah and the mountain and the veil was lifted and He appeared to the mountain, for this is not befitting the attributes of Allah Almighty. The meaning of tajalli in the verse: Abu Mansur says: 'If it is said: How is He seen? It is said: Without modality (bila kayf), for modality pertains to that which has form. Rather, He is seen without the description of standing, sitting, leaning, attachment, connection, separation, facing, backing, shortness, length, darkness, stillness, motion, contact, separation, being outside, nor any meaning that imagination takes or the intellect conceives, for He is exalted above that.'
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the Sunni theologians for the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the Quranic story of Prophet Musa (peace be upon him). The author enumerates five distinct arguments from the verse (7:143). The first argument is that Prophet Musa asked to see Allah, and his request presupposes that Allah is visible; if not, Musa would have been ignorant of his Creator, which is impossible for a prophet. The second argument focuses on Allah's response 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me); He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather negated Musa's seeing at that moment, implying that vision is possible in itself. The third argument is based on the conditional phrase 'if the mountain remains in its place, then you will see Me.' Since the mountain's remaining is a contingent possibility, conditioning vision upon a possible act indicates that vision itself is possible. The author explains that Allah made the mountain level (dakkan) by His own act, showing that the mountain's remaining was possible but Allah chose to destroy it. The fourth argument notes that Allah did not rebuke Musa for asking, unlike His rebuke to Noah and Adam for lesser matters; this leniency indicates that the request was not improper and vision is possible. The fifth argument examines the term 'tajalla' (manifested) to the mountain, explaining that it signifies appearance but without anthropomorphic interpretation; rather, it is an appearance befitting Allah's majesty, without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a quotation from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi emphasizing that divine attributes are not understood by analogy with created beings.

أياس
جهل
حكمة

Checkpoint
Why did Allah not rebuke Musa for asking to see Him, according to the fourth argument?
A) Because Musa was a prophet and could not err.

D) Because the request was hypothetical.

Key Takeaway
Allah's lack of rebuke for Musa's request indicates that seeking vision is permissible and vision is possible.

?

?

?

The Fifth Argument: 'Tajalli' and Seeing Without Modality
Fifth argument based on the term tajalli and the principle of bila kayf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the term 'tajalli' (manifestation) in the verse refers to Allah's appearance to the mountain, but without any anthropomorphic interpretation, and that seeing Allah will be without modality (bila kayf).

Core Idea
Tajalli means appearance, but not like created things; seeing Allah is without how.

The fifth argument examines the word 'tajalla' (manifested) in the verse. The author explains that it means appearance, but this appearance is not like any created being's appearance. The passage concludes with an explanation that Allah will be seen but without modality—without any physical attributes or limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on tajalli
Note that the author defines tajalli as 'appearance' but immediately qualifies that it is not like the appearance of others.
This is an important tanzih (transcendence) point.
2
Understand the negation of anthropomorphism
The author explicitly denies any veil lifting or physical change. The appearance is in a manner befitting Allah.
3
Learn the 'bila kayf' principle
The passage ends with the standard Sunni response to 'how': without modality. Attributes like standing, sitting, etc., do not apply.
This affirms the reality of vision while negating likeness to creation.

إِلَى الْبَيَانِ لأَنَّهُ عَلَى زَعْمِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْمُلْحِدِينَ جَهَلَ اللهَ تَعَالَى وَالْحِكْمَةُ تَقْتَضِي الْبَيَانَ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْبَيَانِ. وَالثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: وَلَكِنِ انظُرْ إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي فَاللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَّقَ الرُّؤْيَةَ بِاسْتِقْرَارِ الْجَبَلِ وَاسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ مِنَ الْجَائِزَاتِ، وَالأَصْلُ أَنَّ تَعْلِيقَ الْفِعْلِ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى جَوَازِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُمْتَنِعُ الْوُجُودِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى امْتِنَاعِهِ وَعَدَمِ تَكَوُّنِهِ، وَتَعْلِيقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ مُتَحَقِّقُ الْوُجُودِ تَحْقِيقٌ لَهُ، وَهَا هُنَا جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ وَهُوَ اسْتِقْرَارُ الْجَبَلِ، وَدَلِيلُ جَوَازِ وُجُودِهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا أَخْبَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُ دَكًّا لَا أَنَّهُ انْدَكَّ بِنَفْسِهِ، وَمَا أَوْجَدَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى كَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يُوجَدَ لَوْ لَمْ يُوجِدْهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى، إِذِ اللهُ تَعَالَى مُخْتَارٌ فِيمَا يَفْعَلُ، فَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْجَبَلَ دَكًّا بِاخْتِيَارِهِ، وَكَانَ جَائِزًا أَنْ لَا يَفْعَلَ دَلَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ جَوَازُ وُجُودِهِ، فَكَانَ تَعْلِيقُ الرُّؤْيَةِ بِهِ دَلِيلَ كَوْنِهَا جَائِزَةً. الرَّابِعُ: أَنَّهُ لَمَّا سَأَلَ الرُّؤْيَةَ مَا أَيَّأَسَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا عَاتَبَهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ خَارِجًا عَنِ الْحِكْمَةِ لَعَاتَبَهُ كَمَا عَاتَبَ نُوحًا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِقَوْلِهِ: إِنِّي أَعِظُكَ أَن تَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَاهِلِينَ حَيْثُ سَأَلَ رَبَّهُ إِنْجَاءَ ابْنِهِ مِنَ الْغَرَقِ. وَكَمَا عَاتَبَ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى أَكْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: أَلَمْ أَنْهَكُمَا عَن تِلْكُمَا الشَّجَرَةِ بَلْ هَذَا أَوْلَى بِالْعِتَابِ، لِأَنَّ هَذَا لَوْ كَانَ جَهْلًا مِنْهُ بِرَبِّهِ لَبَلَغَ رُتْبَةَ الْكُفْرِ وَذَلِكَ لَمْ يَبْلُغْ هَذِهِ الرُّتْبَةَ، وَحَيْثُ لَمْ يُعَاتِبْهُ وَلَمْ يُيَئِّسْهُ بَلْ أَطْمَعَهُ وَرَجَّاهُ حَيْثُ عَلَّقَهُ بِمَا هُوَ جَائِزُ الْوُجُودِ، دَلَّ أَنَّ الرُّؤْيَةَ جَائِزَةُ الْوُجُودِ. الْخَامِسُ: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَالَ: فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ وَالتَّجَلِّي هُوَ الظُّهُورُ أَيْ فَلَمَّا ظَهَرَ رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ. كَذَا رَوَى الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ أَهْلِ التَّأْوِيلِ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: لَكِنْ لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِهِ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ ظُهُورِ غَيْرِهِ. وَكَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ شَيْئًا مِنْ صِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ صِفَاتِ غَيْرِهِ، فَلَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْ هَذَا أَنَّ كَانَ بَيْنَ اللهِ وَبَيْنَ الْجَبَلِ حِجَابٌ فَارْتَفَعَ الْحِجَابُ وَظَهَرَ لِلْجَبَلِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا مِمَّا لَا يَلِيقُ بِصِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى. مَعْنَى التَّجَلِّي فِي الْآيَةِ: يَقُولُ أَبُو مَنْصُورٍ: فَإِنْ قِيلَ كَيْفَ يُرَى؟ قِيلَ بِلَا كَيْفٍ إِذِ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ تَكُونُ لِذِي صُورَةٍ بَلْ يُرَى بِلَا وَصْفِ قِيَامٍ وَقُعُودٍ وَاتِّكَاءٍ وَتَعَلُّقٍ وَاتِّصَالٍ وَانْفِصَالٍ وَمُقَابَلَةٍ وَمُدَابَرَةٍ وَقَصَرٍ وَطَوِيلٍ وَظُلْمَةٍ وَسَاكِنٍ وَمُتَحَرِّكٍ وَمُمَاسٍّ وَتَبَايُنٍ وَخَارِجٍ وَلَا مَعْنَى يَأْخُذُهُ الْوَهْمُ أَوْ يُقَدِّرُهُ الْعَقْلُ لِتَعَالِيهِ عَنْ ذَلِكَ.
The Proof of the People of Truth for Establishing the Vision: As for the People of Truth, they adduced the saying of Allah Almighty, reporting from Musa (peace be upon him): 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You' (7:143). The inference from the verse is in several aspects: First: that Musa (peace be upon him) believed that Allah Almighty is visible; if He were not visible, this would be ignorance of his Creator on his part, and attributing ignorance of Allah to prophets is disbelief. Second: that He Almighty said, 'You will not see Me' (7:143). He negated Musa's seeing Him, but He did not inform that His essence is not visible; for He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather said 'You will not see Me.' If His essence were not visible, He would have informed that it is not visible, for the situation was a situation of need for clarification, because according to the claim of these atheists, he (Musa) would be ignorant of Allah Almighty, and wisdom requires clarification when there is need for clarification. Third: that He Almighty said: 'But look at the mountain; if it should remain in its place, then you will see Me' (7:143). Allah Almighty conditioned vision upon the mountain's remaining, and the mountain's remaining is among contingent things. The principle is that conditioning an act upon what is possible in existence indicates its possibility; conditioning it upon what is impossible in existence indicates its impossibility and non-occurrence; and conditioning it upon what is actualized in existence confirms it. Here, it is possible in existence—that is, the mountain's remaining. The evidence for its possible existence is His saying: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level' (7:143). Allah Almighty informed that He made it level, not that it leveled itself. And what Allah Almighty brings into existence is possible not to exist if Allah Almighty did not bring it into existence, for Allah Almighty is choice in what He does. So when He made the mountain level by His choice, and it was possible for Him not to do so, that indicates its possibility of existence. Thus conditioning vision upon it is evidence that vision is possible. Fourth: that when he asked for vision, Allah Almighty did not make him despair of it nor rebuke him for it. If that had been ignorance of Allah Almighty on his part or outside wisdom, He would have rebuked him, just as He rebuked Noah (peace be upon him) with His saying: 'Indeed, I advise you lest you be among the ignorant' (11:46) when he asked his Lord to save his son from drowning. And just as He rebuked Adam (peace be upon him) for eating from the tree with His saying: 'Did I not forbid you both from that tree?' (7:22). Rather, this is more deserving of rebuke, because if this were ignorance of his Lord, it would reach the level of disbelief, whereas that did not reach this level. And since He did not rebuke him nor make him despair, but rather gave him hope and made him expect by conditioning it upon what is possible in existence, this indicates that vision is possible in existence. Fifth: that He Almighty said: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain' (7:143). Manifestation (tajalli) is appearance—that is, 'when his Lord appeared to the mountain.' Thus narrated Sheikh Abu Mansur from the people of interpretation. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: 'But one does not understand from His appearance what is understood from the appearance of others.' And we say likewise: that nothing of the attributes of Allah Almighty is understood from it what is understood from the attributes of others. So it is not understood from this that there was a veil between Allah and the mountain and the veil was lifted and He appeared to the mountain, for this is not befitting the attributes of Allah Almighty. The meaning of tajalli in the verse: Abu Mansur says: 'If it is said: How is He seen? It is said: Without modality (bila kayf), for modality pertains to that which has form. Rather, He is seen without the description of standing, sitting, leaning, attachment, connection, separation, facing, backing, shortness, length, darkness, stillness, motion, contact, separation, being outside, nor any meaning that imagination takes or the intellect conceives, for He is exalted above that.'
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the Sunni theologians for the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the Quranic story of Prophet Musa (peace be upon him). The author enumerates five distinct arguments from the verse (7:143). The first argument is that Prophet Musa asked to see Allah, and his request presupposes that Allah is visible; if not, Musa would have been ignorant of his Creator, which is impossible for a prophet. The second argument focuses on Allah's response 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me); He did not say 'I am not visible' but rather negated Musa's seeing at that moment, implying that vision is possible in itself. The third argument is based on the conditional phrase 'if the mountain remains in its place, then you will see Me.' Since the mountain's remaining is a contingent possibility, conditioning vision upon a possible act indicates that vision itself is possible. The author explains that Allah made the mountain level (dakkan) by His own act, showing that the mountain's remaining was possible but Allah chose to destroy it. The fourth argument notes that Allah did not rebuke Musa for asking, unlike His rebuke to Noah and Adam for lesser matters; this leniency indicates that the request was not improper and vision is possible. The fifth argument examines the term 'tajalla' (manifested) to the mountain, explaining that it signifies appearance but without anthropomorphic interpretation; rather, it is an appearance befitting Allah's majesty, without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a quotation from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi emphasizing that divine attributes are not understood by analogy with created beings.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that tajalli implies Allah has a physical form or undergoes change.
Correction: The author explicitly denies any bodily interpretation and affirms that Allah's appearance is unlike any other.

Divine Attributes

Fourth Proof: Absence of Rebuke Implies Possibility of Seeing Allah
Nasafi presents the fourth proof for the possibility of seeing Allah based on absence of rebuke.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof for the possibility of seeing Allah, which argues that Allah's lack of rebuke when Musa asked to see Him indicates that such a vision is not impossible.

Core Idea
Allah's silence on Musa's request is proof of its possibility.

This lesson examines a key argument from the Maturidi tradition regarding the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife. The proof is based on the behavior of prophets: when Musa asked to see Allah, he was not rebuked, whereas other prophets were rebuked for lesser requests. This absence of rebuke indicates that the request was not inherently impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the comparisons with Nuh and Adam.
2
Identify the three prophets mentioned
Note that the passage compares Musa's request to the requests of Nuh and Adam, which were rebuked. Understand the context of each.
Nuh asked to save his disbelieving son; Adam ate from the forbidden tree.
3
Analyze the contrast in divine response
Observe that Musa was not rebuked nor made to despair, while Nuh and Adam were rebuked. If Musa's request were ignorance or disbelief, it would have deserved even more severe rebuke.
The argument relies on the principle that Allah does not leave a prophet in ignorance.
4
Understand the logical conclusion
Since no rebuke occurred and Allah gave Musa hope by linking the request to a possible event, it indicates that seeing Allah is a possible occurrence (ja'iz al-wujud).
This is a proof from divine action and consistency.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this proof fits into the larger debate about ru'ya and why the absence of rebuke is considered strong evidence.
It shows that the request was not inherently blameworthy.

والرابع: أنه لما سأل الرؤية ما أيأسه الله تعالى عن ذلك ولا عاتبه عليه، ولو كان ذلك جهلا منه بالله تعالى أو خارجا عن الحكمة لعاتبه كما عاتب نوحا عليه السلام بقوله: إنّى أَعِظُكَ أَن تَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَهِلِينَ حيث سأل ربه إنجاء ابنه من الغرق. وكما عاتب آدم عليه السلام على أكل الشجرة بقوله تعالى: أَلَمْ أَنْهَكُمَا عَن تلكما الشَّجَرَةِ بل هذا أولى بالعتاب، لأن هذا لو كان جهلا منه بربه لبلغ رتبة الكفر وذلك لم يبلغ هذه الرتبة، وحيث لم يعاتبه ولم ييئسه بل أطمعه ورجاه حيث علقه بما هو جائز الوجود، دل أن الرؤية جائزة الوجود.
The fourth: that when he (Musa) asked for vision (ar-ru'ya), Allah did not make him despair of that nor did He rebuke him for it. Had that been ignorance on his part of Allah or outside wisdom, He would have rebuked him as He rebuked Nuh, peace be upon him, by His saying: 'I admonish you lest you be among the ignorant' when he asked his Lord to save his son from drowning. And as He rebuked Adam, peace be upon him, for eating from the tree by His saying: 'Did I not forbid you both from that tree?' Rather, this is more deserving of rebuke, because if this had been ignorance of his Lord, it would have reached the rank of disbelief, while that (the request of Nuh and Adam) did not reach this rank. Since He did not rebuke him nor make him despair, but rather gave him hope and made him expectant by linking it to something whose existence is possible, it indicates that vision (ar-ru'ya) is possible of existence.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) for the theological position that seeing Allah (ru'ya) in the hereafter is possible. The argument follows a pattern of reasoning from the actions of prophets. The author, Nasafi, presents the fourth argument: When Prophet Musa requested to see Allah (as narrated in the Qur'an), Allah did not rebuke him or cause him to despair of that request. If the request had been an act of ignorance about Allah or outside the bounds of wisdom, Allah would have rebuked Musa as He rebuked Prophet Nuh for asking to save his disbelieving son, and as He rebuked Prophet Adam for eating from the forbidden tree. In fact, Musa's request would have been even more deserving of rebuke because it would have bordered on disbelief (kufr). Since Allah did not rebuke Musa but instead gave him hope by linking the request to a possible event (the mountain becoming flat), this proves that seeing Allah is a possible occurrence (ja'iz al-wujud). The argument relies on the principle that Allah does not leave a prophet in ignorance or encourage disbelief; His treatment of Musa indicates the permissibility of the request.

Key Terms
الرؤية (ar-ru'ya)
جواز (jawaz)
عاتب (rebuke)
جهل (ignorance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that since Musa was not rebuked, any request to Allah is permissible, but the context is specific to a request about an attribute of Allah (visibility).
Correction: The proof is limited to the possibility of seeing Allah; it does not imply that every request is acceptable. The absence of rebuke indicates that the request itself is not inherently impossible or ignorant.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the fourth proof for the possibility of seeing Allah?
A) Musa was a great prophet so his request was automatically valid.
B) Allah did not rebuke Musa for asking, unlike other prophets for lesser requests, indicating the request is not inherently impossible.
C) The mountain crumbling proved that seeing Allah is possible.
D) Musa's request was a test of faith.

Key Takeaway
The absence of rebuke for Musa's request demonstrates that seeing Allah is not impossible, unlike other requests that were rebuked.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a du'a to Allah, do you ever pause to consider whether your request reflects proper knowledge of Him or might be born from ignorance? How does Musa's example—where his request was not rebuked—challenge you to examine the nature of your own requests?
?
Allah linked Musa's hope to a possible sign (the mountain becoming flat). Are there areas in your life where you demand immediate answers from Allah without seeking the signs He has placed in your path? What would it mean for you to wait with hope, as Musa did?
?
The argument points to Allah's silence as evidence of permissibility. Is there an area of your life where you have assumed something is forbidden or impossible simply because you haven't seen explicit permission, even though Allah has not rebuked it? How might this lesson change your approach to that area?

The Fifth Proof: Tajalli and the Possibility of Seeing Allah
Nasafi explains the fifth proof based on Allah's تجلي to the mountain and its interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verse about Allah's tajalli to the mountain serves as a proof for the possibility of seeing Allah, and how it is interpreted to avoid anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Allah's manifestation to the mountain is a clear proof that He is visible, but not in a physical sense.

Imam al-Nasafi presents the fifth proof for the possibility of seeing Allah, based on a key Qur'anic verse. The verse speaks of Allah's 'tajalli' to the mountain. Understanding this term correctly is essential, as it could be misinterpreted in an anthropomorphic way. In this lesson, we will follow the argument that leads to the conclusion that Allah is 'mar'iyy' (visible) without compromising His transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms 'tajalli' and 'zuhur'.
The passage is a complete argument from verse to conclusion.
2
Identify the core of the proof
The proof is based on the verse 'When his Lord manifested to the mountain'. The argument hinges on what 'tajalli' means and how it relates to ru'ya.
3
Understand the caution against anthropomorphism
Nasafi quotes Abu Mansur al-Maturidi warning that Allah's manifestation is not like that of created things. No veil or physical appearance is involved.
This preserves tanzih (transcendence).
4
Learn the Ash'ari interpretation
The correct interpretation, from al-Ash'ari via Ibn Furak, is that Allah created life and sight in the mountain so it could see Him. This is supported by another verse about stones falling from fear.
This avoids anthropomorphism while affirming visibility.
5
Conclude that the verse is a clear proof
Thus the verse is a nass (clear textual proof) that Allah is mar'iyy (visible). This is the fifth proof for ru'ya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخامس : أنه تعالى قال : فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ والتجلي هو الظهور أي فلما ظهر ربه للجبل . كذا روى الشيخ أبو منصور عن أهل التأويل قال الشيخ أبو منصور : لكن لا يفهم من ظهوره ما يفهم من ظهور غيره. وكذا نقول: إن شيئا من صفات الله تعالى لا يفهم منه ما يفهم من صفات غيره، فلا يفهم من هذا أن كان بين الله وبين الجبل حجاب فارتفع الحجاب وظهر للجبل لأن هذا مما لا يليق بصفات الله تعالى. فكان معنى التجلي ما حكى أبو بكر محمد بن الحسن بن فورك عن الأشعري أنه قال: إن التجلي أن الله تعالى خلق في الجبل حياة ورؤية حتى رأى ربه. ذكره ابن فورك في تفسيره في تأويل قوله تعالى: وَإِنَّ مِنْهَا لَمَا يَهْبِطُ مِنْ خَشْيَةِ اللَّهِ ولا وجه لحمل الآية إلا على هذا الوجه، وهو نص في إثبات كونه مرئيا، والله الموفق.
The fifth: that He, exalted, said: 'When his Lord manifested (tajalla) to the mountain.' And at-tajalli is manifestation (az-zuhur), i.e., when his Lord appeared to the mountain. Thus narrated Sheikh Abu Mansur from the people of interpretation (ahl at-ta'wil). Sheikh Abu Mansur said: But one does not understand from His manifestation what is understood from the manifestation of others. And likewise we say: Nothing of the attributes of Allah, exalted, is understood from what is understood from the attributes of others. So one does not understand from this that there was a veil between Allah and the mountain that was lifted and He appeared to the mountain, because this is not befitting the attributes of Allah. So the meaning of at-tajalli is what Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak narrated from al-Ash'ari, that he said: At-tajalli is that Allah, exalted, created in the mountain life and sight so that it saw its Lord. Ibn Furak mentioned this in his tafsir in interpreting His saying: 'And indeed among them are some that fall down from fear of Allah.' And there is no way to interpret the verse except in this manner, and it is a clear text (nass) in proving that He is visible (mar'iyy), and Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage is the fifth proof for the possibility of seeing Allah. It is based on the Qur'anic verse, 'And when his Lord manifested (tajalla) to the mountain, He made it crumble to dust' (7:143). First, the author establishes that 'tajalla' means 'zuhur' (appearance or manifestation). Then he quotes Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (probably) cautioning that the appearance of Allah is not like the appearance of created things; we cannot understand it in anthropomorphic terms such as a veil being lifted. Rather, the correct interpretation, as transmitted from al-Ash'ari by Ibn Furak, is that Allah created life and sight in the mountain so that it was able to see its Lord. This interpretation is consistent with another verse where stones fall down from fear of Allah, implying that inanimate objects can be given perception. Therefore, the verse about the mountain is a clear textual proof (nass) that Allah is visible (mar'iyy). The argument moves from the literal wording of the Qur'an to a reasoned interpretation that avoids anthropomorphism while affirming the attribute of visibility.

Key Terms
التجلي (at-tajalli)
الظهور (az-zuhur)
الرؤية (ar-ru'ya)
مرئي (mar'iyy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tajalli means Allah literally removed a veil and physically appeared to the mountain.
Correction: The passage clarifies that this would be anthropomorphic. Instead, Allah created life and sight in the mountain, so it saw Him without any physical change in Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the interpretation of al-Ash'ari cited in the passage, what does 'tajalla' mean in the verse?
A) Allah removed a veil from Himself.
B) Allah created life and sight in the mountain so it saw Him.
C) Allah appeared in a physical form.
D) The mountain saw Allah with its natural eyes.

Key Takeaway
The verse of tajalli, when interpreted correctly, is a clear textual proof that Allah is visible, without compromising His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to see Allah, or is it merely an abstract belief? What would change in your life today if you were certain you will see Him?
?
The mountain was granted life and sight to witness Allah. How does that challenge your idea of what is possible? Are you willing to believe that Allah can make Himself known in ways beyond your imagination—even right now?
?
You have been warned against imagining Allah like creation. Have you ever caught yourself thinking of Allah's attributes in a way that resembles human limitations? What practice can you adopt to purify your understanding?
