Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
Vision is Created by God's Choice
Nasafi presents the principle that vision is created by God and may be absent without physical cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that vision of any object, including divine attributes, depends entirely on God creating sight in the eye, not on the absence of physical barriers.

Core Idea
God creates vision by His choice; He may withhold it even without a screen.

Imam Nasafi begins by establishing a foundational principle: vision is a meaning that God creates in the eye. If He does not create it, a person does not see, even if there is no object blocking the view. This counters the common assumption that physical conditions alone determine sight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi attacks the idea that screens are necessary for non-vision.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the sentence where Nasafi states that vision is a created meaning in the eye. Then see how he uses the possibility that God may not create it to explain non-seeing without screens.
3
Understand the custom argument
Nasafi explains that God's usual custom is to create an opposite of vision when screens exist, but this is a pattern, not a necessity. Reflect on how this distinction matters.
God is not bound by His custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنع سوى إبطال طرق إثبات الأعراض على نفسه، فإذا كانت الرؤية ثابتة وهي معنى في العين بتخليق الله تعالى عرف ذلك بالإجماع من كل، وبالدليل الذي تلجئ أبا هاشم إلى الاعتراف به والله تعالى يخلق ما يخلق باختياره فمن الجائز أن لا يخلق الرؤية في عين إنسان فلا يرى، وإن لم يكن بينه وبين المرئي حجاب لانعدام الرؤية، وهذا كما لم يخلق في حال تحقيق السواتر والحجب وهناك انعدام الرؤية، بأن لم يخلق الله تعالى الرؤية في الآلة، وخلق ضدها لا لوجود السواثر لأن الشيء إنما يستحيل وجوده إذا اشتغل محله بضده، فأما قيام ما ليس بضد للرؤية في غير محل الرؤية فلا يوجب استحالة الرؤية في محلها. غير أن الله تعالى أجرى العادة أن يخلق ضد الرؤية وجود السواتر نظر العباد ليمكنهم إخفاء ما لا يعجبهم اطلاع غيرهم عليه بتحصيل السواتر فيحصل ضد الرؤية في الآلة فلا توجد الرؤية، فلو لم يخلق الرؤية مع انعدام السواتر وارتفاع الحجب في الجواهر والألوان والأكوان (لكانت لا ترى ولا تخرج من كونها جائزة الرؤية) فكذا هذه الأشياء. والذي يحقق هذا أن حركة السفينة لا يراها الراكب ويراها غيره لوجود ضدها في بصره، وإن كانت الحركة مرئية عند الجبائي، وصبغ المغزل والسهم لازم عليه وعلى ابنه والذي يحقق هذا ثبوت رؤية النبي عليه السلام الملك وانعدام رؤية غيره بلا ساتر، ولو لم يكن ذلك إلا بخلق الله الرؤية في عين النبي عليه السلام وخلقه ضد الرؤية في عين غيره. وكذا المحتضر يرى ملك الموت وأعوانه، ومن بحضرته من العواد والممرضين لا يرون شيئا من ذلك. ثبت هذا بأحاديث ينسب رادها وجاحدها إلى الإلحاد والخروج عن الإسلام. فدل أن ما ذهبنا إليه كلام صحيح لا يكاد يتوجه عليه سؤال لو تأمل الخصم وأنصف. وبهذا التحقيق والتقرير يتبين أن الطعوم والروائح وغيرها من الأعراض التي لم يجر الله تعالى العادة برؤيتها مرئية لوجود العلة وهي الوجود وانعدام الرؤية ما كان لاستحالة رؤيتها بل بخلق الله تعالى ضد رؤيتها في أبصارنا، ولو أجرى العادة لرأيناها . والذي يحقق هذا كله أن كلا اتفقوا أن المقابلة للعرض واتصال الشعاع به وقربه وبعده ولطفه مستحيل، إذ هذه المعاني تثبت في الأجسام دون الأعراض. وإذا ثبت هذا علم أن رؤيته لم تكن لوجود المقابلة واتصال الشعاع وقربه، ولم يجز هذه المعاني في حق محل العرض مانعا من إدراك العرض، لأنه أن يكون عدم لو جاز أن تكون العلل التي تعرض لأمكنته مانعة من إدراكه ولا تؤثر فيه بتغيير وصف منه، لم نأمن أن يكون لطف الملائكة وبعد الفلك وعدم اتصال الشعاع بما في قعور البحار وارتفاع المقابلة بين القديم والمحدث ووجود الساتر بين الباري وبيننا مانعا من إدراك ما يوجد بحضرتنا من الفيلة والجمال والفرسان والأعلام وهذا دخول فيما أنكر القوم، ومع ذلك عند اعتراض بعض هذه المعاني محل العرض لا يرى العرض دل أنه إنما لم ير لا لأن هذه المعاني موجبة انعدام الرؤية حق العرض، بل لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق رؤية الأعراض في أبصارنا، ولم يخرج من أن يكون جائز الرؤية، فكذا ما ألزم الخصم.
The prevention is only by invalidating the ways of proving the attributes upon themselves. So if vision is established, and it is a meaning in the eye by the creation of God the Exalted, that is known by consensus from everyone, and by the proof that forces Abu Hashim to acknowledge it. And God the Exalted creates what He creates by His choice; so it is possible that He does not create vision in the eye of a person, and so he does not see, even if there is no screen between him and the visible object, due to the absence of vision. This is like when He did not create [vision] in the case of actual screens and barriers, and there is absence of vision, by God not creating vision in the instrument, and creating its opposite, not due to the existence of screens, because a thing becomes impossible only if its place is occupied by its opposite. As for the existence of what is not opposite to vision in a non-place of vision, it does not necessitate the impossibility of vision in its place. However, God the Exalted has established the custom that He creates the opposite of vision due to the existence of screens for the benefit of servants, so that they can hide what they dislike others knowing, by acquiring screens; then the opposite of vision occurs in the instrument, so vision does not exist. So if He did not create vision while screens are absent and barriers are removed from substances, colors, and accidents, they would not be seen and would not cease to be possible of vision. Likewise for these things. And what verifies this is that the movement of a ship is not seen by the passenger while another sees it, due to the existence of its opposite in his sight, even though movement is visible according to al-Jubba'i; and the spinning of the spindle and the arrow are binding upon him and his son. And what verifies this is the established fact of the Prophet's seeing the angel and the non-seeing of others without a screen; that is only by God's creating vision in the eye of the Prophet and creating the opposite of vision in the eye of another. Likewise, the dying person sees the Angel of Death and his helpers, while those present among visitors and caretakers see nothing of that. This is established by hadiths whose rejecter and denier is attributed to heresy and departure from Islam. So it shows that what we hold is sound speech that no objection can be directed against if the opponent would reflect and be fair. And by this investigation and exposition, it becomes clear that tastes, smells, and other accidents for which God the Exalted has not established the custom of seeing are visible due to the existence of the cause, which is existence; and the absence of vision is not due to the impossibility of seeing them, rather due to God the Exalted creating the opposite of their vision in our eyes; and if He had established the custom, we would see them. And what verifies all this is that everyone agrees that facing an accident, connection of rays with it, its nearness, distance, and subtlety are impossible, for these meanings are established in bodies, not accidents. And when this is established, it is known that its vision was not due to the existence of facing, connection of rays, or nearness; and it is not permissible that these meanings in the case of the locus of the accident be a preventer of perceiving the accident, because if it were permissible that the causes that occur to its place prevent its perception and do not affect it by changing any of its attributes, we would not be safe from [the possibility] that the subtlety of angels, the distance of the celestial sphere, the lack of ray connection concerning what is in the depths of the seas, the absence of facing between the Eternal and the originated, and the existence of a screen between the Creator and us, would prevent the perception of what exists in our presence of elephants, camels, horsemen, and flags; and this is an entry into what the people denied. And yet, when some of these meanings intervene in the locus of the accident, the accident is not seen. This indicates that it is not seen not because these meanings necessitate the absence of vision of the accident, but because God the Exalted did not create vision of accidents in our eyes, and it does not cease to be possible of vision. So likewise what the opponent has imposed.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument defending the Maturidi position that the vision of God and attributes is possible and depends solely on God's creation of sight in the eye, not on physical conditions like screens, distance, or direction. The author begins by stating that the objection to vision is only invalid if one rejects the ways of proving attributes. He asserts that vision is a meaning created by God in the eye, known by consensus and a proof that forces even Abu Hashim to admit it. God creates by choice, so He may not create vision in a person's eye, resulting in non-seeing even without a screen. This is like when God does not create vision despite actual screens, due to creating an opposite of vision in the instrument. The author clarifies that a thing becomes impossible only if its place is occupied by its opposite; the presence of something non-opposite in a different place does not prevent vision. Moreover, God's custom is to create the opposite of vision when screens exist, so that people can hide things. If God did not create vision even when screens are absent, then substances, colors, and accidents would not be seen, yet they remain possible of vision. The author then gives examples: the passenger on a ship does not see its motion while another does, due to the presence of an opposite in the passenger's eye; the Prophet saw the angel while others did not without any screen; the dying person sees the Angel of Death while others do not. These are verified by hadiths, whose rejection constitutes heresy. Thus the author's position is sound. He then extends the argument: tastes, smells, and other accidents are visible in principle because they exist; we do not see them because God has not created sight for them in our eyes, not because they are inherently invisible. Finally, the author argues that everyone agrees that physical relations like facing, ray connection, nearness, etc., are impossible for accidents, as they apply only to bodies. Therefore, vision of accidents is not due to such conditions, and these conditions cannot be preventers. If they were preventers, then the subtlety of angels, distance of the sky, etc., would prevent us from seeing nearby large objects, which is absurd. The fact that when these conditions intervene the accident is not seen shows that the non-vision is due to God's not creating sight, not the physical conditions themselves. So the opponent's objection fails.

Key Terms
رؤية
ضد
السواتر
التخليق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person does not see an object because the object is blocked by a screen or because the eye is not properly oriented.
Correction: Nasafi argues that non-seeing is ultimately due to God not creating vision in the eye, even when no screen exists; screens are simply occasions for God's custom of creating an opposite.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the real reason a person does not see an object when a screen is present?
A) The screen physically blocks the light
B) God creates an opposite of vision in the eye
C) The object becomes invisible
D) The eye lacks the power to see through screens

Key Takeaway
Vision depends entirely on God's creative act; screens or their absence do not necessitate seeing or not seeing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Every time you open your eyes, do you recognize that you are witnessing a direct act of God's creation? If you truly believed that your sight is sustained moment by moment by His will, how would your gratitude and reliance on Him change starting today?
?
Have you ever assumed that your ability to see something was automatic or guaranteed? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what practical step can you take to remind yourself that your vision is a gift that God could withdraw at any moment?
?
If God can withhold vision even when no screen exists, what does that imply about your spiritual perception? Are there truths you choose not to 'see' because you rely on your own reasoning rather than seeking God's creation of understanding in your heart? What will you do to ask Him to create clarity?

Divine Attributes
intermediate

Examples Confirm Vision Depends on God's Creation
Nasafi provides empirical and prophetic evidence for his claim about vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how everyday examples and prophetic traditions confirm that sight is granted by God alone, not by physical conditions.

Core Idea
Examples show that vision varies by God's will, not by screens or distance.

Nasafi now reinforces his argument with concrete examples: a ship passenger does not see the ship's motion while others do, the Prophet saw the angel without any screen while others did not, and a dying person sees the Angel of Death while bystanders see nothing. These cases prove that vision is a direct gift from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the examples in the passage
Identify the three main examples: ship motion, Prophet and angel, dying person. Note the common pattern: one sees, another does not, with no physical difference.
Each example highlights that God creates sight for one and withholds it from another.
2
Understand the reasoning behind each example
For each, Nasafi explains that the difference is due to God creating vision or its opposite. Reflect on how this supports the principle from Lesson 1.
3
Consider the authority of hadith
Nasafi mentions that rejecting these hadiths is close to heresy. Notice how he uses religious authority to strengthen his case.
This underscores the importance of these narrations in Muslim theology.

المنع سوى إبطال طرق إثبات الأعراض على نفسه، فإذا كانت الرؤية ثابتة وهي معنى في العين بتخليق الله تعالى عرف ذلك بالإجماع من كل، وبالدليل الذي تلجئ أبا هاشم إلى الاعتراف به والله تعالى يخلق ما يخلق باختياره فمن الجائز أن لا يخلق الرؤية في عين إنسان فلا يرى، وإن لم يكن بينه وبين المرئي حجاب لانعدام الرؤية، وهذا كما لم يخلق في حال تحقيق السواتر والحجب وهناك انعدام الرؤية، بأن لم يخلق الله تعالى الرؤية في الآلة، وخلق ضدها لا لوجود السواثر لأن الشيء إنما يستحيل وجوده إذا اشتغل محله بضده، فأما قيام ما ليس بضد للرؤية في غير محل الرؤية فلا يوجب استحالة الرؤية في محلها. غير أن الله تعالى أجرى العادة أن يخلق ضد الرؤية وجود السواتر نظر العباد ليمكنهم إخفاء ما لا يعجبهم اطلاع غيرهم عليه بتحصيل السواتر فيحصل ضد الرؤية في الآلة فلا توجد الرؤية، فلو لم يخلق الرؤية مع انعدام السواتر وارتفاع الحجب الرؤية في عين غيره. وكذا المحتضر يرى ملك الموت وأعوانه، ومن بحضرته من العواد والممرضين لا يرون شيئا من ذلك. ثبت هذا بأحاديث ينسب رادها وجاحدها إلى الإلحاد والخروج عن الإسلام. فدل أن ما ذهبنا إليه كلام صحيح لا يكاد يتوجه عليه سؤال لو تأمل الخصم وأنصف. وبهذا التحقيق والتقرير يتبين أن الطعوم والروائح وغيرها من الأعراض التي لم يجر الله تعالى العادة برؤيتها مرئية لوجود العلة وهي الوجود وانعدام الرؤية ما كان لاستحالة رؤيتها بل بخلق الله تعالى ضد رؤيتها في أبصارنا، ولو أجرى العادة لرأيناها . والذي يحقق هذا كله أن كلا اتفقوا أن المقابلة للعرض واتصال الشعاع به وقربه وبعده ولطفه مستحيل، إذ هذه المعاني Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If there is no screen, everyone should be able to see the same object.

Checkpoint
Why does the passenger on a ship not see the ship's motion according to Nasafi?
A) The motion is too fast for the eye
B) There is a screen blocking the view
C) God creates an opposite of vision in the passenger's eye
D) The passenger is not looking in the right direction

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your ability to see right now is a direct creation of God every instant? How would your gratitude change if you lived with that awareness today?
?
The passenger was blind to the ship's movement because God did not create vision for it. What spiritual realities—like God's mercy, signs of His power, or the nearness of death—might you be blind to because God has not yet created vision in your heart? Will you ask Him to do so?
?
The Prophet saw what others could not. Are you content with ordinary sight, or do you long for the insight that sees the unseen? Commit to one concrete action today that proves you live by faith, not by physical sight alone.

Divine Attributes
advanced
7 min
Physical Conditions Do Not Cause Vision of Accidents
Nasafi argues that accidents are visible potentially, and non-seeing is due to God's act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that accidents like tastes and smells are in principle visible, but we do not see them because God has not created that sight, not because of inherent impossibilities like facing or ray connection.

Core Idea
Accidents are visible in essence; non-seeing is due to God's will, not physical impossibilities.

Nasafi extends his principle to all accidents: tastes, smells, colors, etc. He argues that these are visible because they exist, and that the conditions people usually associate with vision—like facing, ray connection, distance—are not applicable to accidents. Therefore, our failure to see them is solely because God has not created sight for them in our eyes.

Guided Path
1
Read the final argument
Read from 'وبهذا التحقيق والتقرير' to the end. Notice how Nasafi shifts from examples to a logical argument about the nature of accidents.
This part refutes the idea that physical conditions are necessary for vision.
2
Understand the argument about causes
Nasafi argues that if physical conditions could prevent vision, then we would not see large objects due to things like distance or subtlety—which is absurd. So those conditions cannot be preventers.
3
See the conclusion
The final point: accidents are not seen because God did not create vision of them, but they remain possible of vision. This applies to the opponent's objection as well.
The argument is symmetric for divine attributes.

الجبائي، وصبغ المغزل والسهم لازم عليه وعلى ابنه والذي يحقق هذا ثبوت رؤية النبي عليه السلام الملك وانعدام رؤية غيره بلا ساتر، ولو لم يكن ذلك إلا بخلق الله الرؤية في عين النبي عليه السلام وخلقه ضد الرؤية في عين غيره. وكذا المحتضر يرى ملك الموت وأعوانه، ومن بحضرته من العواد والممرضين لا يرون شيئا من ذلك. ثبت هذا بأحاديث ينسب رادها وجاحدها إلى الإلحاد والخروج عن الإسلام. فدل أن ما ذهبنا إليه كلام صحيح لا يكاد يتوجه عليه سؤال لو تأمل الخصم وأنصف. وبهذا التحقيق والتقرير يتبين أن الطعوم والروائح وغيرها من الأعراض التي لم يجر الله تعالى العادة برؤيتها مرئية لوجود العلة وهي الوجود وانعدام الرؤية ما كان لاستحالة رؤيتها بل بخلق الله تعالى ضد رؤيتها في أبصارنا، ولو أجرى العادة لرأيناها . والذي يحقق هذا كله أن كلا اتفقوا أن المقابلة للعرض واتصال الشعاع به وقربه وبعده ولطفه مستحيل، إذ هذه المعاني تثبت في الأجسام دون الأعراض. وإذا ثبت هذا علم أن رؤيته لم تكن لوجود المقابلة واتصال الشعاع وقربه، ولم يجز هذه المعاني في حق محل العرض مانعا من إدراك العرض، لأنه أن يكون عدم لو جاز أن تكون العلل التي تعرض لأمكنته مانعة من إدراكه ولا تؤثر فيه بتغيير وصف منه، لم نأمن أن يكون لطف الملائكة وبعد الفلك وعدم اتصال الشعاع بما في قعور البحار وارتفاع المقابلة بين القديم والمحدث ووجود الساتر بين الباري وبيننا مانعا من إدراك ما يوجد بحضرتنا من الفيلة والجمال والفرسان والأعلام وهذا دخول فيما أنكر القوم، ومع ذلك عند اعتراض بعض هذه المعاني محل العرض لا يرى العرض دل أنه إنما لم ير لا لأن هذه المعاني موجبة انعدام الرؤية حق العرض، بل لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق رؤية الأعراض في أبصارنا، ولم يخرج من أن يكون جائز الرؤية، فكذا ما ألزم الخصم.
The prevention is only by invalidating the ways of proving the attributes upon themselves. So if vision is established, and it is a meaning in the eye by the creation of God the Exalted, that is known by consensus from everyone, and by the proof that forces Abu Hashim to acknowledge it. And God the Exalted creates what He creates by His choice; so it is possible that He does not create vision in the eye of a person, and so he does not see, even if there is no screen between him and the visible object, due to the absence of vision. This is like when He did not create [vision] in the case of actual screens and barriers, and there is absence of vision, by God not creating vision in the instrument, and creating its opposite, not due to the existence of screens, because a thing becomes impossible only if its place is occupied by its opposite. As for the existence of what is not opposite to vision in a non-place of vision, it does not necessitate the impossibility of vision in its place. However, God the Exalted has established the custom that He creates the opposite of vision due to the existence of screens for the benefit of servants, so that they can hide what they dislike others knowing, by acquiring screens; then the opposite of vision occurs in the instrument, so vision does not exist. So if He did not create vision while screens are absent and barriers are removed from substances, colors, and accidents, they would not be seen and would not cease to be possible of vision. Likewise for these things. And what verifies this is that the movement of a ship is not seen by the passenger while another sees it, due to the existence of its opposite in his sight, even though movement is visible according to al-Jubba'i; and the spinning of the spindle and the arrow are binding upon him and his son. And what verifies this is the established fact of the Prophet's seeing the angel and the non-seeing of others without a screen; that is only by God's creating vision in the eye of the Prophet and creating the opposite of vision in the eye of another. Likewise, the dying person sees the Angel of Death and his helpers, while those present among visitors and caretakers see nothing of that. This is established by hadiths whose rejecter and denier is attributed to heresy and departure from Islam. So it shows that what we hold is sound speech that no objection can be directed against if the opponent would reflect and be fair. And by this investigation and exposition, it becomes clear that tastes, smells, and other accidents for which God the Exalted has not established the custom of seeing are visible due to the existence of the cause, which is existence; and the absence of vision is not due to the impossibility of seeing them, rather due to God the Exalted creating the opposite of their vision in our eyes; and if He had established the custom, we would see them. And what verifies all this is that everyone agrees that facing an accident, connection of rays with it, its nearness, distance, and subtlety are impossible, for these meanings are established in bodies, not accidents. And when this is established, it is known that its vision was not due to the existence of facing, connection of rays, or nearness; and it is not permissible that these meanings in the case of the locus of the accident be a preventer of perceiving the accident, because if it were permissible that the causes that occur to its place prevent its perception and do not affect it by changing any of its attributes, we would not be safe from [the possibility] that the subtlety of angels, the distance of the celestial sphere, the lack of ray connection concerning what is in the depths of the seas, the absence of facing between the Eternal and the originated, and the existence of a screen between the Creator and us, would prevent the perception of what exists in our presence of elephants, camels, horsemen, and flags; and this is an entry into what the people denied. And yet, when some of these meanings intervene in the locus of the accident, the accident is not seen. This indicates that it is not seen not because these meanings necessitate the absence of vision of the accident, but because God the Exalted did not create vision of accidents in our eyes, and it does not cease to be possible of vision. So likewise what the opponent has imposed.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument defending the Maturidi position that the vision of God and attributes is possible and depends solely on God's creation of sight in the eye, not on physical conditions like screens, distance, or direction. The author begins by stating that the objection to vision is only invalid if one rejects the ways of proving attributes. He asserts that vision is a meaning created by God in the eye, known by consensus and a proof that forces even Abu Hashim to admit it. God creates by choice, so He may not create vision in a person's eye, resulting in non-seeing even without a screen. This is like when God does not create vision despite actual screens, due to creating an opposite of vision in the instrument. The author clarifies that a thing becomes impossible only if its place is occupied by its opposite; the presence of something non-opposite in a different place does not prevent vision. Moreover, God's custom is to create the opposite of vision when screens exist, so that people can hide things. If God did not create vision even when screens are absent, then substances, colors, and accidents would not be seen, yet they remain possible of vision. The author then gives examples: the passenger on a ship does not see its motion while another does, due to the presence of an opposite in the passenger's eye; the Prophet saw the angel while others did not without any screen; the dying person sees the Angel of Death while others do not. These are verified by hadiths, whose rejection constitutes heresy. Thus the author's position is sound. He then extends the argument: tastes, smells, and other accidents are visible in principle because they exist; we do not see them because God has not created sight for them in our eyes, not because they are inherently invisible. Finally, the author argues that everyone agrees that physical relations like facing, ray connection, nearness, etc., are impossible for accidents, as they apply only to bodies. Therefore, vision of accidents is not due to such conditions, and these conditions cannot be preventers. If they were preventers, then the subtlety of angels, distance of the sky, etc., would prevent us from seeing nearby large objects, which is absurd. The fact that when these conditions intervene the accident is not seen shows that the non-vision is due to God's not creating sight, not the physical conditions themselves. So the opponent's objection fails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accidents are inherently invisible due to their nature.
Correction: Nasafi argues they are visible because they exist; we just lack the God-given capacity to see them.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why do we not see tastes and smells?
A) They are not visible by nature
B) They are too subtle for the eye
C) God has not created sight for them in our eyes
D) They lack existence

Key Takeaway
Accidents are in principle visible; our non-seeing of them is due to God's will, not physical impossibilities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If physical conditions are not the real cause of whether we see something, but rather God's will creates vision directly, what does that imply about your reliance on physical explanations for spiritual blindness? Are you waiting for a 'sign' or a 'facing' with God, when the obstacle is not external but His withholding of vision? What would it take for you to truly acknowledge that God is in control of your perception of truth, and not the circumstances around you? Spend five minutes today asking Allah to remove the barrier of your own making and grant you vision of His signs.
?
The opponent uses the lack of physical conditions to argue that God cannot be seen. Nasafi shows that those conditions are irrelevant. Are you using 'logical' excuses to avoid accepting truths that would require you to change? What 'physical conditions' are you hiding behind to avoid confronting the reality of Allah's commands? Commit to one area where you will stop making excuses and directly seek Allah's creation of that understanding in your heart.
?
This passage teaches that non-seeing is due to Allah's will, not inherent impossibility. Reflect: In your own life, is there something of Allah's creation or truth that you fail to perceive because of your own preconceived notions of how it 'should' be? How can you align your expectations with the reality that Allah does as He wills, and that includes opening or closing your spiritual eyes? Make a sincere du'a today asking Allah to show you the truth as truth and grant you the ability to follow it.

The Maturidi Position on Seeing God and Refutation of Al-Qalanisi's Theory
The author states the majority Maturidi position and discusses Al-Qalanisi's alternative view with refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority Maturidi stance on seeing God in this world and why they reject al-Qalanisi's underlying principle about the impossibility of preventing nature from its action.

Core Idea
The Maturidis accept both weakness and creation of an opposite as possible causes for not seeing God.

This passage delves into a nuanced debate within the Maturidi school about why God is not seen in this world. While al-Qalanisi, a fellow theologian, proposed a single explanation based on weak eyesight, the majority Maturidis offer two valid possibilities. The author explains al-Qalanisi's reasoning and then refutes the cornerstone of his argument, revealing the Maturidi commitment to theological flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: majority view, al-Qalanisi's view, his rationale, and the refutation.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two positions
First, locate the majority Maturidi position (alluded to by al-Maturidi himself). Then find al-Qalanisi's alternative and why he chose it.
Al-Qalanisi rejected the 'creation of opposite' theory.
3
Understand al-Qalanisi's rationale
Al-Qalanisi believed that a strong eye must naturally see; preventing it by creating an opposite would violate the nature of vision. This stems from his doctrine of 'generated acts' (al-mutawallidāt).
This is the key point that the Maturidis reject.
4
Grasp the Maturidi refutation
The Maturidis argue that it is possible for vision to be absent either by weakness or by creating an opposite in a strong eye. They reject al-Qalanisi's principle about the impossibility of preventing nature.
Thus they can repel opponents using either explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى هذا الجواب ذهب أكثر أصحابنا وإليه يشير الشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي رحمه الله. رأي القلانسي في الرؤية وذهب أبو العباس القلانسي من جملة متكلمي أهل الحديث أنه تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصار الخلق في الدنيا فإذا أراد إكرامهم بالرؤية خلق في أبصارهم قوة، وهذا الجواب مستقيم مقنع إذ كم من شيء مرئي لا يدركه الإنسان لضعف في بصره، ولهذا يتفاوت الناس في رؤية الأشياء عند الدقة والبعد، ثم هو إنما تعلق بهذا الجواب دون الأول لأن من مذهبه أن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر ممتنع إذ من مذهبه أن منع ذي الطبع عن فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال على مذهبه المعروف أن المتولدات فعل الله تعالى بإيجاب الطبع. وهذا الأصل عندنا غير صحيح، فيجوز عندنا انعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوته، ويجوز أيضا امتناعها لضعف في البصر. فيجوز لنا دفع إلزام الخصوم بامتناع الرؤية للحال بالطريقين جميعا وعنده لا يجوز ذلك إلا بالطريق الثاني على ما بينا
To this answer the majority of our companions inclined, and to it Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, may God have mercy on him, alludes. The opinion of al-Qalanisi concerning vision: Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi, among the theologians of the People of Hadith, held that He Most High is not seen in this world due to weakness in the sight of creatures in this world. When He desires to honor them with vision, He creates strength in their eyesight. This answer is sound and convincing, for many visible things are not perceived by a person due to weakness in his sight, and for this reason people differ in seeing things at close range and at a distance. Then he adhered to this answer rather than the first because according to his doctrine, the removal of vision by creating its opposite in the eyesight while the eyesight is strong is impossible, since according to his doctrine, preventing a nature from its action while the nature remains is impossible, based on his well-known doctrine that generated acts are the act of God Most High by necessitation of nature. This principle is not correct according to us. For us, it is permissible that vision be absent by creating its opposite in the eyesight while it is strong, and it is also permissible that it be absent due to weakness in the eyesight. So we can repel the opponents' objection concerning the impossibility of vision in the present state by both paths, while according to him it is not permissible except by the second path, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage first records the majority Maturidi position: most of the author's companions (aṣḥābunā) adopted the second answer (that God's vision is not customary in this world) as alluded to by Imam al-Maturidi. Then the author presents the view of Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi, a theologian from the People of Hadith. Al-Qalanisi argued that God is not seen in this world due to weakness (ḍu'f) in human eyesight. When God wishes to honor people with vision (in the afterlife), He creates strength (quwwa) in their eyes. The author acknowledges that this answer is sound and convincing, citing the everyday experience that many visible things are not perceived due to weak sight, and people differ in visual acuity. The author then explains why al-Qalanisi preferred this answer over the first answer (the creation of an opposite of vision in the eye). Al-Qalanisi believed that it is impossible for vision to be removed by creating an opposite in the eye while the eye retains its natural strength, because according to his doctrine, it is impossible to prevent a nature (ṭab') from its action while the nature remains. This is based on his well-known principle that generated acts (al-mutawallidāt) are God's act through the necessitation of nature (ījāb al-ṭab'). The author then refutes this principle: 'This principle is not correct according to us' (hādhā al-aṣl 'indanā ghayr ṣaḥīḥ). The Maturidis hold that it is permissible for vision to be absent either through the creation of an opposite in a strong eye or through weakness in the eye. Therefore, the Maturidis can refute the opponents' objection regarding the impossibility of vision in this world using both paths, whereas al-Qalanisi can only use the second path (weakness).

Key Terms
الرؤية
ضعف البصر
ضد الرؤية
المتولدات
الطبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Maturidis completely reject al-Qalanisi's view that weak eyesight prevents vision of God.
Correction: The Maturidis actually accept weak eyesight as one valid explanation, but they also allow the creation of an opposite as another, and they reject al-Qalanisi's principle that prevents the latter.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Qalanisi reject the first answer (creating an opposite of vision) for explaining why God is not seen in this world?
A) Because he believed it is impossible to create an opposite of vision.
B) Because he held that it is impossible to prevent a nature from its action while the nature remains.
C) Because he thought the first answer contradicts the Quran.
D) Because he believed weak eyesight is the only possible cause.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis maintain flexibility in explaining why God is not seen in this world, accepting both weakness and the creation of an opposite as valid possibilities, while rejecting al-Qalanisi's rigid principle about nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qalanisi clung to his principle about nature, even though it limited his options. Is there a theological or personal principle you hold so tightly that it restricts how you see God's power and wisdom? What would it cost you to let it go?
?
The Maturidis accept two valid explanations for why we do not see God in this world. When you face a difficulty in your faith that you cannot fully understand, do you insist on one explanation, or are you willing to hold multiple possibilities in humility? What does your answer reveal about your trust in God's wisdom?
?
Imagine you are standing before God, and He asks you why you refused to accept that He could have created an opposite in your eyes while they were strong. What would your answer be, based on how you approach His attributes today?

Al-Qalanisi's View on Vision of Allah and the Maturidi Response
Al-Nasafi presents al-Qalanisi's view on ru'ya and the Maturidi response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qalanisi's position on the beatific vision (ru'ya), his reasoning based on his doctrine of generated acts, and how the Maturidi school critiques and offers an alternative explanation.

Core Idea
Al-Qalanisi explains that we don't see Allah now due to weak sight, not impossibility.

In this passage, al-Nasafi presents the view of al-Qalanisi on the beatific vision, distinguishing it from the Maturidi alternative. Al-Qalanisi argues that vision of Allah is possible in the afterlife but prevented in this world by human weakness, not by any inherent impossibility. He rejects the idea that Allah could create a contrary in the sight to prevent vision, based on his theory of generated acts. The author then offers the Maturidi critique, showing how they allow both explanations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the two possible explanations for not seeing Allah.
2
Identify al-Qalanisi's main claim
Find where al-Qalanisi states that Allah is not seen in this world due to weakness in human sight, and what he says about the afterlife.
He affirms that Allah can be seen in the afterlife by creating strength in sight.
3
Understand why he rejects the first answer
Note the reason al-Qalanisi gives for not accepting the explanation that vision is prevented by creating a contrary in the sight. Connect this to his doctrine of generated acts (mutawallidāt).
He believes it is impossible to prevent a natural action while the nature remains.
4
Examine the Maturidi critique
Read how al-Nasafi responds: the Maturidis consider al-Qalanisi's principle unsound. They allow both possibilities—creating a contrary or weakness.
This shows the Maturidi position that Allah's power is not constrained by natures.
5
Reflect on the difference
Consider how the two schools differ: al-Qalanisi's view is tied to his theory of generated acts, while Maturidis affirm divine omnipotence more directly.
This impacts how they answer objections about ru'ya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي القلانسي في الرؤية وذهب أبو العباس القلانسي من جملة متكلمي أهل الحديث أنه تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصار الخلق في الدنيا فإذا أراد إكرامهم بالرؤية خلق في أبصارهم قوة، وهذا الجواب مستقيم مقنع إذ كم من شيء مرئي لا يدركه الإنسان لضعف في بصره، ولهذا يتفاوت الناس في رؤية الأشياء عند الدقة والبعد، ثم هو إنما تعلق بهذا الجواب دون الأول لأن من مذهبه أن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر ممتنع إذ من مذهبه أن منع ذي الطبع عن فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال على مذهبه المعروف أن المتولدات فعل الله تعالى بإيجاب الطبع. وهذا الأصل عندنا غير صحيح، فيجوز عندنا انعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوته، ويجوز أيضا امتناعها لضعف في البصر. فيجوز لنا دفع إلزام الخصوم بامتناع الرؤية للحال بالطريقين جميعا وعنده لا يجوز ذلك إلا بالطريق الثاني على ما بينا
The opinion of al-Qalanisi on vision: And Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi, among the theologians of the people of hadith, went that He, exalted, is not seen in this world due to weakness in the sight of the creatures in this world. So when He wishes to honor them with vision, He creates strength in their sight. And this answer is sound and convincing, for how many visible things does man not perceive due to weakness in his sight, and for this people differ in seeing things when they are fine and distant. Then he adhered to this answer rather than the first because his doctrine is that the removal of vision by creating its opposite in the sight while the sight is strong is impossible, since his doctrine is that preventing a possessor of a nature from its act while its nature remains is impossible according to his known doctrine that generated acts are the act of Allah by necessitation of nature. And this principle is not sound with us, so with us the absence of vision is allowed by creating its opposite in the sight while it is strong, and also its prevention due to weakness in sight is allowed. So it is permissible for us to repulse the opponents' objection regarding the impossibility of vision in the present state by both ways, while according to him it is not permissible except by the second way, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage presents the view of al-Qalanisi on the vision of Allah (ru'ya). It begins by stating his position that Allah is not seen in this world due to weakness in human sight, but when Allah wishes to honor believers with vision in the afterlife, He creates strength in their sight. The author notes that this answer is sound, using the analogy of visible objects that humans cannot perceive due to weak sight. The passage then explains why al-Qalanisi adopted this answer instead of the first (the Maturidi answer that vision is prevented by creating a contrary in the sight): because al-Qalanisi believes that it is impossible to prevent a natural action while the nature remains, based on his doctrine that generated acts (mutawallidāt) are acts of Allah by necessitation of nature. Then the author (al-Nasafi) objects that this principle is not sound according to the Maturidis; they allow both possibilities: absence of vision by creating a contrary in the sight while it is strong, or prevention due to weakness. Thus Maturidis can refute the objection via both ways, while al-Qalanisi only via the second. This shows a nuanced discussion of the mechanisms of ru'ya.

Key Terms
رؤية
القلانسي
الطبع
المتولدات
ضد
بصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Qalanisi denies the possibility of ru'ya entirely or that he says Allah cannot be seen at all.
Correction: Al-Qalanisi affirms that Allah will be seen in the afterlife; he only denies it in this world due to human weakness, not impossibility.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qalanisi, why is Allah not seen in this world?
A) Because it is impossible for Allah to be seen
B) Because of weakness in human sight
C) Because sight cannot perceive the infinite
D) Because Allah does not wish to be seen

Key Takeaway
Al-Qalanisi's view on ru'ya hinges on his doctrine of generated acts, leading him to attribute the absence of vision to human weakness alone, while Maturidis maintain that Allah can prevent vision by either creating weakness or a contrary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe you cannot see Allah now—but do you truly live as if His presence is veiled by your own weakness, or do you use that as an excuse for spiritual laziness?
?
Al-Qalanisi says you don't see Allah because your sight is weak. Are you actively seeking to strengthen your 'sight'—through knowledge, worship, and purification—so that you may be worthy of vision in the hereafter?
?
If Allah’s power is absolutely free (as Maturidis hold), what does that mean for your own excuses about why you fall short? Are you hiding behind your own nature when you could be asking for transformation?

Refuting the Infinite Regress Objection to Seeing Allah
al-Nasafi refutes the objection that absence of ru'ya due to a contrary implies infinite regress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi scholars answer the objection that the absence of ru'ya due to a contrary leads to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Two answers stop the regress: prevention as ignorance, and two mutual preventers.

The objection that if Allah is not seen because of a contrary in our sight, then that contrary itself requires a contrary ad infinitum, seems compelling. However, Maturidi scholars provide two elegant responses that dissolve the regress without contradiction. Let's examine the objection and the answers carefully.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first line of the source passage carefully. The objector argues that absence of vision due to a contrary implies an endless chain of contraries.
Notice the structure: 'if it is said...' introduces the objection.
2
Explore the first answer
Read the first response: prevention (man‘) is like ignorance of a thing, which does not entail infinite ignorances. Consider how this stops the regress.
The analogy is key: ignorance of X is also ignorance of itself, and that is a single ignorance.
3
Examine the second answer
Read the second response: Allah creates two preventers that mutually prevent each other. This ends the chain without infinite regress.
This answer uses the idea of mutual prevention to stop at two.
4
Note the dismissal of the body claim
The author quickly dismisses the claim that vision is related to the body, saying it has already been refuted earlier.
This part is not expanded here; it refers to previous arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: لو كان لا يرى لقيام ضد رؤيته في أبصارنا وذلك الضد موجود فيجوز أن يرى، فلم يكن عدم رؤيته إلا بضد لرؤيته، وكذا في حق الثاني والثالث إلى ما لا يتناهى. قلنا: من أصحابنا من قال ذلك المنع منع عن رؤيته ومن رؤية نفسه، كالجهل بالشيء جهل به وبنفسه ولهذا يجعل الجهل ولا يلزم جهالات غير متناهية. ومنهم من قال يخلق الله تعالى فيه ممتنعين كل واحد منهما منع عن صاحبه. فأما دعواهم أن الرؤية متعلقة بالجسم فقد بينا فساده.
If it is said: If He were not seen because of the existence of a contrary of His vision in our sight, and that contrary exists, then it is possible that He is seen, so His not being seen would only be due to a contrary to His vision, and likewise for the second and third ad infinitum. We say: Among our companions, one said that that prevention prevents vision of Him and vision of itself, like ignorance of a thing: ignorance of it and of itself, and for this ignorance is [considered one] and infinite ignorances are not entailed. And among them, one said that Allah creates in it two preventers, each preventing the other. As for their claim that vision is related to the body, we have already shown its falsity.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and two answers concerning the vision of Allah. The objector argues: If Allah is not seen due to a contrary (didd) in our sight, then that contrary exists, so it is possible that if the contrary were absent, He would be seen. Then the absence of vision would always be due to a contrary, leading to an infinite regress of contraries. The response: Two answers from Maturidi scholars. First, the prevention (man') of vision is like ignorance: ignorance of a thing also involves ignorance of itself, and that does not entail infinite ignorances; similarly, the prevention of vision prevents both seeing Allah and seeing the prevention itself, so no infinite regress. Second, Allah creates in the sight two mutually exclusive preventers, each preventing the other, stopping the regress. Then the author dismisses the claim that vision is related to the body as already refuted.

Key Terms
ضد
منع
جهل
ممتنعين
لا يتناهى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection implies an infinite regress of contraries that cannot be escaped.
Correction: The Maturidi answers show that the regress stops either by analogy with ignorance (which does not entail infinite ignorances) or by Allah creating two mutual preventers.

Checkpoint
How does the first Maturidi answer avoid infinite regress?
A) By denying the existence of contraries
B) By comparing prevention to ignorance, which does not entail infinite ignorances
C) By claiming vision is impossible
D) By limiting contraries to two

Key Takeaway
Maturidi scholars refute the infinite regress objection by either analogizing prevention to ignorance or positing two mutually exclusive preventers, both stopping the chain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a divine attribute that your mind cannot fully grasp, like the seeing of Allah in the afterlife, do you immediately object with your limited logic, or do you admit your ignorance and submit? Will you practice saying 'Allah knows best' the next time such a doubt arises?
?
The objector assumes that what is not seen does not exist. Where in your own life have you denied Allah's existence or care because you did not see Him with your physical eyes? Are you ready to seek Him through His signs and revelations instead of your senses?
?
The first answer compares the prevention of vision to ignorance: one is ignorant of the thing and of one's own ignorance. Are you aware of your own ignorance regarding Allah's essence and attributes? Will you ask Allah to increase you in beneficial knowledge and protect you from arrogant certainty?

Al-Nasafi's Critique of al-Jubba'i on Vision
Al-Nasafi refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that vision relates to bodies, colors, and accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's argument that al-Jubba'i and his son erred by relating vision to mere existence instead of the true cause, and how this error leads to anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Focusing on existence without cause leads to anthropomorphism.

In this passage, al-Nasafi responds to the Mu'tazilite position on vision, specifically the claims of al-Jubba'i and his son that vision relates to bodies, colors, and accidents. He identifies a critical flaw: they consider only the existence of these entities, not the cause of vision. This superficial approach, he argues, mirrors the methodology of anthropomorphists. Al-Nasafi then turns the tables on the Mu'tazila, who accuse Ahl al-Sunna of tashbih, showing that their own reasoning is flawed.

Guided Path

2
Contrast existence with cause
Notice how al-Nasafi criticizes them for relating vision by 'mere existence' (mujarrad al-wujud) while neglecting the cause (al-illa). Understand why this is a methodological error.
The cause is the underlying reason why vision is possible.
3
Link to anthropomorphists
See how al-Nasafi connects this error to the method of the mujassima (anthropomorphists). Reflect on why ignoring causes leads to superficial theology.
4
Examine the counter-accusation

The passage cuts off; contemplate the intended reply.

As for the statement of al-Jubba'i: that it (vision) is related to bodies, colors, and accidents. And the statement of his son: that it is related to bodies and colors. That from them is a relation by mere existence (mujarrad al-wujud) without the cause (al-illa), for they looked at what vision is related to, not the cause. And relation by mere existence and turning away from the reality of the cause is the foundation of the anthropomorphists (mujassima). And by such appears the deviation of the Mu'tazila from causes and realities and their clinging to what exists from the aspect of the apparent, like the act of the ignorant among the anthropomorphists and anthropopathists (mushabbiha) and others. And it is imagined by the novice (al-ribd) that what they are upon is from the realm of realities because his deficient intellect stops at it. Commentary
This passage refutes the positions of al-Jubba'i and his son regarding the object of vision (ru'ya). Two Opinions on Denying Ru'ya in Maturidi Kalam
Nasafi presents two school opinions on denying ru'ya and refutes the body claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi scholars addressed the objection that denying ru'ya leads to infinite ignorance.

Core Idea
Denying ru'ya does not entail infinite ignorance; the school offers two consistent alternatives.

In this passage, Nasafi presents two internal opinions within his school that resolve a potential logical problem arising from the denial of the beatific vision. The problem is that if someone cannot see Allah, does that mean they are ignorant of Him in an infinite way? Nasafi shows how his school avoids this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the two opinions and the final refutation.
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Understand the first opinion (prevention like ignorance)
The first opinion holds that prevention from seeing God also prevents self-knowledge, analogous to ignorance. This avoids infinite ignorance because ignorance is a single thing.
The analogy with ignorance is key to avoiding infinite regress.
3
Understand the second opinion and the refutation
The second opinion states that Allah creates two preventions that block each other. Then note the refutation of the claim that vision is related to the body, which was already shown false.
Both opinions provide coherent alternatives to the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا: من أصحابنا من قال ذلك المنع منع عن رؤيته ومن رؤية نفسه، كالجهل بالشيء جهل به وبنفسه ولهذا يجعل الجهل ولا يلزم جهالات غير متناهية. ومنهم من قال يخلق الله تعالى فيه ممتنعين كل واحد منهما منع عن صاحبه. فأما دعواهم أن الرؤية متعلقة بالجسم فقد بينا فساده.
We said: Some of our companions said that that prevention is prevention from seeing Him and from seeing oneself, like ignorance of a thing is ignorance of it and of itself, and because of that ignorance is considered [one] and infinite ignorances are not entailed. And some of them said: Allah the Exalted creates in him two preventions, each one of them preventing from its counterpart. As for their claim that vision is related to the body, we have already shown its falsity.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage presents two opinions within the author's school (the Maturidi school) regarding the argument that denying the vision of God (ru'ya) leads to an infinite regress of ignorances. The first opinion holds that the prevention (al-man') from seeing God also prevents self-knowledge, analogous to ignorance: being ignorant of something implies ignorance of that thing and of oneself, but this does not entail multiple infinite ignorances. The second opinion states that Allah creates two preventions in the person, each preventing the other, so there is no infinite chain. The author then restates that the Mu'tazilite claim that vision is restricted to bodies has already been refuted. The passage demonstrates the internal coherence of the Ash'ari/Maturidi position on ru'ya.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying ru'ya leads to an infinite regress of ignorances, making the position incoherent.
Correction: The Maturidi school offers two coherent alternatives: either prevention is like ignorance (one ignorance) or Allah creates two preventions that block each other, avoiding infinite regress.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Critique of Relying on Pure Existence and Mu'tazila Inconsistency
Nasafi criticizes opponents for ignoring the cause of visibility and Mu'tazila hypocrisy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi criticizes the opponents for ignoring the underlying cause of visibility and how he exposes the Mu'tazila as falling into anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Empirical observation without causal analysis leads to inconsistency.

In this passage, Nasafi continues his critique of those who deny the vision of Allah by arguing that they rely solely on empirical observation without seeking the rational cause. He then points out the self-contradictory stance of the Mu'tazila, who inadvertently fall into anthropomorphism themselves. The passage highlights a key methodological failing in theological argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the two main criticisms.
Note the proverb at the end; it summarizes the Mu'tazila's situation.
2
Identify the two criticisms
The passage contains two separate but related critiques. Find where each begins and what it targets.
First critique: opponents rely on pure existence without cause. Second critique: Mu'tazila are inconsistent.
3
Understand the fallacy of ignoring the cause
Nasafi argues that the opponents' reasoning is flawed because they base their conclusion on empirical observation in the physical world (shahid) without seeking the underlying 'illa (cause). This leads to an incorrect analogy.
4
Analyze the Mu'tazila inconsistency
The Mu'tazila disagreed with anthropomorphists on one issue (agent being body) but agreed on vision based on mere existence. This inconsistency shows they fell into tashbih.
5
Reflect on the proverb
The proverb 'She cast her own disease upon me and slipped away' means the Mu'tazila accused others of anthropomorphism but committed it themselves. Consider how this reinforces the critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنهم اعتمدوا على الوجود المحض، وقالوا: وجدنا في الشاهد أن الرؤية تتعلق بهذه الأجناس المخصوصة من غير النظر إلى العلة والتميز بينها وبين الأوصاف الإضافية التي هي أوصاف الوجود، وجعلوا مجرد الوجود في دعواهم أن كل فاعل جسم على ما مر في تلك المسألة، ولم ينظروا إلى العلة. والمعتزلة خالفتهم في تلك المسألة ثم صوبتهم في مسألة الرؤية في مجرد الوجود. فيتبين في الحقيقة وعند التأمل أنهم هم المشبهة حيث صوبتهم في تلك المسألة وجلسوا تحت المثل السائر "رمتني بدائها وانسلت".
Then they relied on pure existence, and said: We found in the witnessed world that vision applies to these specific kinds without consideration of the cause and the distinction between them and the relational attributes which are attributes of existence, and they made mere existence in their claim that every agent is a body as passed in that issue, and they did not look to the cause. And the Mu'tazila disagreed with them in that issue, then agreed with them in the issue of vision concerning mere existence. So it becomes clear in truth and upon reflection that they (the Mu'tazila) are the anthropomorphists, since they agreed with them in that issue and sat under the proverbial saying: 'She cast her own disease upon me and slipped away.'
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage contains two criticisms. First, the author criticizes the opponents (likely the anthropomorphists or those who deny vision) for relying on empirical observation (shahid) without seeking the underlying cause (illa). They merely note that vision occurs on specific kinds in the physical world and assume that's the rule, ignoring that the cause of visibility is something else (namely existence). They also inconsistently claim that every agent is a body. Second, the author points out the inconsistency of the Mu'tazila: they disagreed with the anthropomorphists on one issue but agreed with them on the issue of vision, thus themselves falling into tashbih. The proverb means they accuse others of their own fault.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming that empirical observation from the physical world (shahid) is sufficient to determine the possibility of divine attributes without considering the underlying cause.
Correction: Nasafi teaches that rational inquiry must seek the cause (illa) and cannot rely solely on empirical patterns. Ignoring the cause leads to faulty analogies and theological errors.

Key Takeaway

?

?
The Mu'tazila accused others of anthropomorphism but fell into it themselves. Where in your life have you condemned flaws in others while ignoring the same flaws in yourself? Will you ask Allah for the humility to see your own faults first?

Nasafi's Argument: Vision of God from Existence Alone
Nasafi argues that Mu'tazila are like Mushabbiha and proves vision from existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's logical argument that the Mu'tazila inadvertently agree with anthropomorphists on the vision of God, and that vision is based on existence, not physical categories.

Core Idea
Vision of God follows from His existence, not from being a body or substance.

Nasafi here uses a clever logical analogy to expose an inconsistency in the Mu'tazila position on the vision of God. He shows that by limiting vision to specific categories, they fall into the same trap as the anthropomorphists, and then he provides a proof that vision is rooted in the simple fact of existence, which avoids all such limitations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the accusation
Read the opening lines where Nasafi claims the Mu'tazila, by agreeing with the Mushabbiha on the issue of vision in mere existence, become themselves the Mushabbiha. Notice the proverbial saying he quotes.
This sets up the polemical tone.
2
Follow the analogy
Nasafi presents a conditional argument: if someone limits vision to specific genera, then by the same logic existence could be limited, leading to absurd consequences (negation of God, Christians saying He is substance, Mujassima saying He is body). Trace this analogy carefully.
The analogy shows the need for an absolute cause.
3
Identify the absolute cause
Nasafi states that the absolute cause of vision is being existent (being موجود). He also argues that substance is not visible because it is a substance, and similarly colors and spatial states. This clears the way for vision of what is beyond these genera.
Existence itself is the common factor.
4
See the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that by grasping these meanings, the consistency of Ahl al-Haqq and the contradictions of the Qadariyya become clear. Reflect on how this argument distinguishes truth from falsehood.
This is the broader theological payoff.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and then try to explain the analogy in your own words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعتزلة خالفتهم في تلك المسألة ثم صوبتهم في مسألة الرؤية في مجرد الوجود. فيتبين في الحقيقة وعند التأمل أنهم هم المشبهة حيث صوبتهم في تلك المسألة وجلسوا تحت المثل السائر: رمتني بدائها وانسلت. ثم لو جاز لقائل أن يقول: إن الرؤية تعلقت بهذه الأجناس المخصوصة، فلا يكون ما وراءها مرئيا، لجاز لقائل أن يقول: إن الموجود أجناس مخصوصة وهي الأعراض، وأعيان وهي الجواهر والأجسام، فلا يكون ما وراءها موجودا، فتنفي المعطلة الصانع لخروجه عن هذه الأجناس، وتزعم النصارى أنه جوهر لكونه موجودا ليس بجسم ولا عرض، وتزعم المجسمة أنه جسم لكونه موجودا ليس بعرض ولا جوهر، ولا محيص لهم عن هذا، ولابد لهم من الرجوع إلى إثبات العلة المطلقة للرؤية، وليس ذلك إلا ما بينا من كونه موجودا، وإلى بيان أن الجوهر ليس بمرئي لأنه جوهر تعلقها بما وراءه، وكذا الألوان والأكوان. فيتبين حينئذ جواز رؤية ما وراء هذه الأجناس، كما أنا إذا بينا أن الجسم ما كان موجودا لكنه جسما لوجود ما ليس بجسم موجودا، وكذا في الجوهر والعرض لم يكن بد من الرجوع إلى بيان حد للموجود يشمل الكل، فحينئذ يتبين جواز موجود ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا عرض. وبالوقوف على مثل هذه المعاني تبين استمرار أصول أهل الحق واندفاع التناقض عنها، واضطراب أصول القدرية وكثرة تمكن التناقض فيها. وبهذا يمتاز الحق من الباطل والصحيح من الفاسد.
The Mu'tazila disagreed with them (the Mushabbiha) on that issue, then they agreed with them on the issue of vision in mere existence. So it becomes clear in reality and upon reflection that they are the Mushabbiha, since they agreed with them on that issue and sat under the proverbial saying: 'She threw me with her disease and slipped away.' Then if it were permissible for a claimant to say: 'Vision is related to these specific genera, so what is beyond them is not visible,' it would be permissible for a claimant to say: 'Existence is specific genera, namely accidents, and entities, namely substances and bodies, so what is beyond them does not exist'; thus the Mu'attila would negate the Creator because of His being beyond these genera, the Christians would claim He is a substance because He exists not as a body or accident, and the Mujassima would claim He is a body because He exists not as an accident or substance; and they have no escape from this. They must return to establishing the absolute cause of vision, which is nothing but what we have explained: His being existent, and to the demonstration that the substance is not visible because it is a substance (vision relates to what is beyond it), and likewise colors and spatial states. Then it becomes clear the permissibility of seeing what is beyond these genera, just as when we demonstrate that the body is something that exists but is a body because of the existence of what is not a body, and similarly for substance and accident, one must return to establishing a definition of existence that encompasses all; then the permissibility of an existent that is not substance, body, or accident becomes clear. By grasping such meanings, the continuity of the principles of the people of truth and the repulsion of contradiction from them become clear, as well as the confusion of the principles of the Qadariyya and the frequency of contradiction in them. And by this truth is distinguished from falsehood and the correct from the corrupt.
Source pages p. 635

Commentary
This passage is a polemical argument by Nasafi against the Mu'tazila regarding the vision of God. He begins by stating that the Mu'tazila disagreed with the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) on some other issue, but then agreed with them on the issue of vision of God in mere existence. This makes them, in truth, like the Mushabbiha, despite their claims otherwise. Nasafi then uses a logical analogy (in the form of a conditional argument) to show the absurdity of limiting vision to specific categories. If someone claims that vision only pertains to specific genera (like bodies, substances, etc.) and thus what is beyond them is not visible, then by the same reasoning existence could be limited to specific genera, and whatever is beyond them would not exist. This would lead to contradictory positions: the Mu'attila would deny the Creator, the Christians would say He is a substance, and the Mujassima would say He is a body. The only way out is to recognize that vision is caused by existence itself, not by being within a genus. He then elaborates that just as we show that a body exists through a common definition of existence, we can show that an existent beyond these categories is possible. Through such reasoning, the consistency of Ahl al-Haqq (people of truth) becomes clear, as well as the contradictions in the Qadariyya (i.e., Mu'tazila). This distinguishes truth from falsehood.

Key Terms
الرؤية
المشبهة
المعتزلة
العلة المطلقة
الموجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Vision of God requires a body or direction, or something that fits within the usual categories of sight.
Correction: Nasafi argues that vision is based on existence, not on being within a certain genus like body or substance. Thus God, who is existent, can be seen even though He is not a body or substance.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi identify as the absolute cause ('illa mutlaqa) of vision?
A) Being a body
B) Being a substance
C) Being existent
D) Being in a place

Key Takeaway
The absolute cause of vision is existence, not any physical category, so God, who is existent, is visible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Nasafi equates agreeing with Mu'tazila on vision to being like Mushabbiha. Where in your own beliefs have you unconsciously agreed with false assumptions while thinking you are correct? What must change?
?
The passage shows that small errors in logic lead to massive contradictions like denying God's existence. What small compromises in your understanding of God's attributes have you made that, if followed through, could lead to dangerous conclusions? Commit to rooting out error.

Refuting the Pointing Objection to God's Visibility
Nasafi refutes the first Mu'tazili objection linking visibility to pointing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazili objection that visibility requires pointing fails, and how Nasafi counters it.

Core Idea
Pointing is not a necessary condition for visibility.

Nasafi now addresses a specific argument from the Mu'tazila: that if God were visible, He could be pointed to. Since He cannot, He cannot be seen. Nasafi gives two responses and then turns the tables with a counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first answer
Read the Mu'tazili claim and Nasafi's first response, which invokes the Ash'ari position that pointing to God is allowed without direction.
The Ash'aris permit pointing to God, so the objection does not apply to them.
2
Understand Nasafi's own stance
Nasafi follows al-Qalanisi in holding that God is not pointed to, but he argues that pointing is not a condition for visibility; it is due to being spatially located.
Pointing is an attribute of existence, not a prerequisite for visibility.
3
Grasp the counter-argument
Nasafi turns the objection back on the Mu'tazila: since God is a command-giver (addressee), and in the witnessed world every command-giver can be pointed to, the Mu'tazila would have to admit God can be pointed to, contradicting their own denial.
This refutes their objection by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه أخرى والرد عليها. ثم لهم أسئلة فاسدة تندفع كلها بمعرفة ما بينا من الأصل نذكر بعضها ليسهل الوقوف على كيفية الدفع - بعون الله تعالى ومشيئته. منها أنهم يقولون: كل مرئي يجوز أن يشار إليه والله تعالى لو كان مرئيا لكان يجوز أن يشار إليه. والجواب عنه: أن بعض أصحاب الرؤية وهم الأشعرية يجوزون الإشارة إلى الله تعالى لا إلى جهة كما تجوز الرؤية لا في جهة فكان الإلزام عنهم مندفعا. ثم عندنا وإن كان لا يشار إليه، وإليه ذهب أبو العباس القلانسي، ولكن في الشاهد ما كان جواز الإشارة إلى شيء لجواز الرؤية بل لكونه متحيزا في جهة، فكان جواز الإشارة مع وجود الرؤية من أوصاف الوجود فبطل الإلزام. ثم يعارضون فيقال لهم: كل مخاطب آمر ناه في الشاهد يشار إليه، فلو كان الله تعالى مخاطبا آمرا ناهيا لكان يشار إليه. فما أجابوا به عنه فهو لهم جواب. ومن ذلك قولهم: كل مرئي في مكان. فيقال لهم ما كان في المكان لأنه مرئي، وما كان مرئيا لأنه في مكان، فإنه تعالى لو خلق جزء لا يتجزأ لا في مكان لكان مرئيا والصفحة العليا من العالم مرئية وهي لا في مكان، وقد يحل في المكان ما ليس بمرئي عندكم، كالعلوم والقدر والإرادات وغيرها فبطل قولهم.
Other doubts and their refutation. Then they have corrupt questions all repelled by knowing the principle we explained; we mention some to facilitate understanding of the method of refutation - with the help of Allah Most High and His will. Among them is their saying: 'Every visible thing can be pointed to, and if God were visible, He could be pointed to.' The answer to it: Some of the proponents of vision, namely the Ash'aris, permit pointing to God Most High but not towards a direction, just as they permit vision without direction, so the objection from them is repelled. Then according to us, even if He is not pointed to - and this is the position of Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi - still, in the witnessed world, the permissibility of pointing to a thing is not due to the permissibility of vision, but due to its being spatially located in a direction; so the permissibility of pointing along with the existence of vision is among the attributes of existence, and thus the objection falls. Then they are countered by saying: 'Every addressee who commands and forbids in the witnessed world can be pointed to, so if God is an addressee who commands and forbids, He should be pointed to.' Whatever they answer to that is an answer to themselves. And among that is their saying: 'Every visible thing is in a place.' It is said to them: It is not in the place because it is visible, nor is it visible because it is in a place. Indeed, if He created an indivisible part not in a place, it would be visible; and the upper surface of the world is visible yet not in a place; and something may reside in a place that is not visible in your view, like knowledge, power, wills, and others. So their saying falls.
Source pages p. 635

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two specific objections raised by the Mu'tazila against the vision of God. Nasafi introduces these objections as corrupt questions that are easily repelled once his earlier principle (that vision depends on existence) is understood. The first objection claims that everything visible can be pointed to, and since God cannot be pointed to, He cannot be visible. Nasafi gives two answers: First, the Ash'aris actually permit pointing to God without direction, just as they permit vision without direction, so the objection does not apply to them. Second, according to Nasafi's own position (following al-Qalanisi), even if God is not pointed to, the connection between vision and pointing is not necessary; in the witnessed world, pointing is due to being spatially located, not due to visibility. He then uses a counter-argument: since God is a command-giver (auditor, speaker), and in the witnessed world every command-giver can be pointed to, the Mu'tazila would have to admit that God can be pointed to, which they deny; thus they contradict themselves. The second objection claims that every visible thing is in a place. Nasafi refutes it by showing that visibility is not caused by being in a place; an indivisible part created nowhere could be visible, the upper surface of the world is visible yet not in a place, and many things that are in a place (like knowledge) are not visible. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
الإشارة
القلانسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Visibility necessarily implies being pointable.
Correction: Pointing is an attribute of spatial existence, not a condition for visibility; God is visible without being pointable.

Checkpoint
What is the first Mu'tazili objection that Nasafi refutes?
A) That God cannot be seen because He is not a body
B) That every visible thing can be pointed to, so God cannot be seen
C) That vision is an attribute of deficiency
D) That the world is a body and cannot see God

Key Takeaway
Pointing is not a necessary condition for visibility; the Mu'tazili objection fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to hope for the vision of God in the afterlife, but what does your attachment to the physical pleasures of this world say about your true desire? Is your longing for the sight of God as intense as your longing for the next meal or the next success?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected the vision of God because it seemed to imply physical limitations. Are there any divine attributes or actions of Allah that you find difficult to accept because they do not fit your rational expectations? Will you submit your intellect to revelation, or will you continue to reshape God to fit your own reasoning?
?
Nasafi uses the fact that God commands as an argument against the Mu'tazila. When you hear Allah's commands in the Qur'an, do you respond with immediate obedience, or do you first require intellectual satisfaction? What does your reaction reveal about your real commitment to divine authority?

Refuting the Place Objection to God's Visibility
Nasafi refutes the second Mu'tazili objection linking visibility to place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why being in a place is not a requirement for visibility, using Nasafi's arguments.

Core Idea
Visibility does not depend on being in a place.

The second Mu'tazili objection claims that every visible thing is in a place, so God cannot be seen. Nasafi refutes this by providing counterexamples: an indivisible part created nowhere, the upper surface of the world, and non-visible things in places.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Mu'tazili claim that everything visible is in a place, implying God cannot be seen.
2
Examine the first two counterexamples
Nasafi points out an indivisible part created nowhere would be visible, and the upper surface of the world is visible yet not in a place.
These show visibility does not require place.
3
Consider the third counterexample
Nasafi notes that things like knowledge and power reside in a place but are not visible, proving place does not guarantee visibility.
This further breaks the link between place and visibility.
